{"code":1,"isDone":false,"toInsertArticleList":[{"createdTime":"2021-09-28 00:55:06","updatedTime":"2021-09-28 00:55:06","title":"Blue Floats Away: A Tender Illustrated Fable About Our Capacity for Change, Told Through the Story of Water","link":"https://www.brainpickings.org/?p=74384","description":"<h3>In praise of our unfathomed capacity to experience beautiful new things beyond our habitual ideas of the possible.</h3>\n<hr>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Blue-Floats-Away-Travis-Jonker/dp/1419744232/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\"><img width=\"320\" height=\"409\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/bluefloatsaway.jpg?fit=320%2C409&#38;ssl=1\" class=\"cover alignright size-medium\" alt=\"Blue Floats Away: A Tender Illustrated Fable About Our Capacity for Change, Told Through the Story of Water\" loading=\"lazy\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/bluefloatsaway.jpg?w=900&#38;ssl=1 900w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/bluefloatsaway.jpg?resize=320%2C409&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/bluefloatsaway.jpg?resize=600%2C767&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/bluefloatsaway.jpg?resize=240%2C307&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/bluefloatsaway.jpg?resize=768%2C981&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 320px) 100vw, 320px\" /></a></p><p>&#8220;The things we want are transformative, and we don’t know or only think we know what is on the other side of that transformation,&#8221; Rebecca Solnit wrote in her unsurpassable <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2014/08/04/field-guide-to-getting-lost-rebecca-solnit/\"><em>Field Guide to Getting Lost</em></a>. </p>\n<p>This might be the greatest challenge of our consciousness &#8212; that when life beckons us to broaden our inner landscapes of possibility, it calls on us to choose experiences the transformative power of which we might not be able to recognize and desire with the yet-untransformed self, and so we might not choose to have them. (Philosophers have explored this paradoxical blind spot to transformative experiences in an elegant thought experiment known as <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2017/09/13/transformative-experience-vampire-problem/\">the vampire problem</a>.) </p>\n<p>But this might also be the most hopeful aspect of our consciousness &#8212; that we know ourselves only incompletely; that the life we have is only a subset of our possible life; that we are capable of having experiences which profoundly transform how we live our lives in this house of sinew and soul, transforming in the process the very texture of who we believe ourselves to be.</p>\n<p>This paradox of transformation comes alive with uncommon tenderness, through a singular lens &#8212; the science and poetics of Earth&#8217;s water cycle &#8212; in <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Blue-Floats-Away-Travis-Jonker/dp/1419744232/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><strong><em>Blue Floats Away</em></strong></a> (<a href=\"https://www.worldcat.org/title/blue-floats-away/oclc/1244438345&#038;referer=brief_results\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><em>public library</em></a>) by <strong>Travis Jonker</strong>, an elementary school librarian by day and an author by night, and <strong>Grant Snider</strong>, an orthodontist by day and an artist (yes, <a href=\"https://explore.brainpickings.org/tagged/grant-snider\">that</a> artist) by night.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Blue-Floats-Away-Travis-Jonker/dp/1419744232/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" /></a></p>\n<p>But just as he begins understanding the currents and devising a way to ride them back home, the unimaginable happens &#8212; Little Blue melts into the tropical waters and becomes part of the ocean.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Blue-Floats-Away-Travis-Jonker/dp/1419744232/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" he marvels at the aurora borealis as he drifts poleward across the night sky. </p>\n<p>And then, as the air grows colder and the latitude higher, Little Blue suddenly starts growing bigger and bigger, until snowflakes begin to shed from him as the winds return him to his original Northern homeland.</p>\n<p><a /></a></p>\n<p>Although the story ends on the classic happy-ending note of a fairy tale &#8212; Little Blue, in his cloud embodiment, is reunited with his parents &#8212; Jonker takes care to cast no false enchantment. On the final page, an author&#8217;s note details the science of Earth&#8217;s increasingly precarious water cycle and urges the young reader to counter climate change with daily actions that even a child could take &#8212; those seemingly simple but profound transformations of habit on the individual level that, across the sweep of time and generations, shape the transformation of consciousness on the civilizational level. </p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Blue-Floats-Away-Travis-Jonker/dp/1419744232/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/bluefloatsaway20.jpg?resize=680%2C453&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"453\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-74394\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/bluefloatsaway20.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/bluefloatsaway20.jpg?resize=320%2C213&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/bluefloatsaway20.jpg?resize=600%2C400&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/bluefloatsaway20.jpg?resize=240%2C160&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/bluefloatsaway20.jpg?resize=768%2C512&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a></p>\n<p>Complement <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Blue-Floats-Away-Travis-Jonker/dp/1419744232/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><strong><em>Blue Floats Away</em></strong></a> with Ellen Meloy on <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2021/08/10/ellen-meloy-turquoise-water/\">water as a portal to transcendence</a> and <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2019/12/10/what-color-is-night-grant-snider/\"><em>What Color Is Night</em></a> &#8212; Snider&#8217;s solo serenade to the nocturnal blues &#8212; then revisit the world&#8217;s most poetic marine biologist on <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2021/06/07/rachel-carson-the-edge-of-the-sea/\">the ocean and the meaning of life</a>.</p>\n<hr /><h3>donating = loving</h3><p class=\"flipboard-keep\">For 15 years, I have been spending hundreds of hours and thousands of dollars each month to keep <em>Brain Pickings</em> going. +0000","feedId":17,"bgimg":"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/bluefloatsaway.jpg?fit=320%2C409&ssl=1","linkMd5":"a801628255fd369905ea6b521abeaced","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn100@2020_6/2021/09/27/16-55-26-042_8a9e8a4ca5904a6c.webp","destWidth":320,"destHeight":409,"sourceBytes":14588,"destBytes":14588,"author":"Maria Popova","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/bluefloatsaway.jpg?fit=320%2C409&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn100@2020_6/2021/09/27/16-55-26-042_8a9e8a4ca5904a6c.webp","https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/bluefloatsaway1.jpg?resize=680%2C440&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn91@2020_1/2021/09/27/16-55-33-190_bdbd2435c88332f4.webp","https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/bluefloatsaway21.jpg?resize=680%2C453&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn69@2020_2/2021/09/27/16-55-34-518_54e128de851a4b17.webp","https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/bluefloatsaway2.jpg?resize=680%2C440&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx27/cdn83@2020_6/2021/09/27/16-55-33-338_9abf5808d60faeed.webp","https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/bluefloatsaway4.jpg?resize=680%2C440&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn95@2020_1/2021/09/27/16-55-33-741_8bf06d0a9cf2aaf1.webp","https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/bluefloatsaway3.jpg?resize=680%2C440&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx31/cdn92@2020_6/2021/09/27/16-55-34-351_19e003e5a7b3fffa.webp","https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/bluefloatsaway22.jpg?resize=680%2C453&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn84@2020_1/2021/09/27/16-55-34-212_20a70e444b0c51b5.webp","https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/bluefloatsaway6.jpg?resize=680%2C440&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn81@2020_3/2021/09/27/16-55-34-722_9379a62e24fcea75.webp","https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/bluefloatsaway5.jpg?resize=680%2C440&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn46@2020_3/2021/09/27/16-55-35-583_dd13da238cec5799.webp","https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/bluefloatsaway7.jpg?resize=680%2C440&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx31/cdn64@2020_6/2021/09/27/16-55-33-160_f59e94109c9e0b34.webp","https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/bluefloatsaway8.jpg?resize=680%2C442&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx5oss/cdn54@2020_3/2021/09/27/16-55-34-471_1ad55a6d9e75ec81.webp","https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/bluefloatsaway9.jpg?resize=680%2C443&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx5oss/cdn16@2020_5/2021/09/27/16-55-33-212_4b5e264b7e1d5f0e.webp","https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/bluefloatsaway23.jpg?resize=680%2C453&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn15@2020_6/2021/09/27/16-55-33-909_4dfec559196851e9.webp","https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/bluefloatsaway20.jpg?resize=680%2C453&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn3@2020_2/2021/09/27/16-55-33-616_e5d7eff6aa74d30b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/brainpickings/rss/~4/wcDbi1HSqNE":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn32@2020_6/2021/09/27/16-55-33-375_68caa4ca12eac6d8.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1632761706657},{"createdTime":"2021-09-28 00:55:06","updatedTime":"2021-09-28 00:55:06","title":"Einstein’s Dreams: Physicist Alan Lightman’s Poetic Exploration of Time and the Antidote to the Anxiety of Aliveness","link":"https://www.brainpickings.org/?p=74241","description":"<h3>&#8220;A life in the past cannot be shared with the present. Each person who gets stuck in time gets stuck alone.&#8221;</h3>\n<hr>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Einsteins-Dreams-Alan-Lightman/dp/140007780X/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\"><img width=\"320\" height=\"495\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/einsteinsdreams_lightman.jpg?fit=320%2C495&#38;ssl=1\" class=\"cover alignright size-medium\" alt=\"Einstein&#8217;s Dreams: Physicist Alan Lightman&#8217;s Poetic Exploration of Time and the Antidote to the Anxiety of Aliveness\" loading=\"lazy\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/einsteinsdreams_lightman.jpg?w=775&#38;ssl=1 775w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/einsteinsdreams_lightman.jpg?resize=320%2C495&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/einsteinsdreams_lightman.jpg?resize=600%2C927&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/einsteinsdreams_lightman.jpg?resize=240%2C371&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/einsteinsdreams_lightman.jpg?resize=768%2C1187&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 320px) 100vw, 320px\" /></a></p><p>&#8220;When you realize you are mortal,&#8221; the poet, painter, and philosopher Etel Adnan wrote <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2019/02/06/etel-adnan-journey-to-mount-tamalpais/\">while regarding a mountain</a>, &#8220;you also realize the tremendousness of the future.&#8221; A decade earlier, shortly before a heart attack severed her life-time, Hannah Arendt observed in her superb Gifford Lectures lectures on <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2015/12/02/hannah-arendt-the-life-of-the-mind-time-thinking/\">the life of the mind</a> that our finitude, &#8220;set in an infinity of time stretching into both past and future, constitutes the infrastructure, as it were, of all mental activities.&#8221; While Arendt was composing these thoughts and silent cells were barricading one of her arteries, Ursula K. Le Guin was composing her novelistic inquiry into <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2018/10/10/ursula-k-le-guin-the-dispossessed-time/\">what it means to live responsibly</a>, observing: “If time and reason are functions of each other, if we are creatures of time, then we had better know it, and try to make the best of it.&#8221; A generation before her, Borges had formulated <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2016/09/19/a-new-refutation-of-time-borges/\">the ultimate declaration of our temporal creatureliness</a>, declaring: “Time is the substance I am made of. Time is a river which sweeps me along, but I am the river; it is a tiger which destroys me, but I am the tiger; it is a fire which consumes me, but I am the fire.” </p>\n<p>Half a century of neuroscience and psychology have confirmed the physical fact beneath the poetic sentiment &#8212; we now know that our experience of time is <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2017/09/04/alan-burdick-why-time-flies-empathy/\">the crucible of empathy</a> and <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2019/07/19/altered-states-of-consciousness-marc-wittmann/\">the defining dimension of personal identity</a>.</p>\n<figure  class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/discus-chronologicus-german-time-model-from-the-1720s_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/07/DiscusChronologicus_small.jpg?resize=680%2C728&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"728\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-74249\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/07/DiscusChronologicus_small.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/07/DiscusChronologicus_small.jpg?resize=320%2C342&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/07/DiscusChronologicus_small.jpg?resize=600%2C642&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/07/DiscusChronologicus_small.jpg?resize=240%2C257&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/07/DiscusChronologicus_small.jpg?resize=768%2C822&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\"><em>Discus chronologicus</em> &#8212; a German depiction of time from the early 1720s, included in <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2012/02/07/cartographies-of-time/\"><em>Cartographies of Time</em></a>. (Available as <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/discus-chronologicus-german-time-model-from-the-1720s_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">a print</a> and as <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/discus-chronologicus-german-time-model-from-the-1720s_wall-clock?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">a wall clock</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>The young clerk at the Bern patent office was thinking about none of this in the spring of 1905, the spring of a new century still verdant with possibility, when he dreamt up his general relativity &#8212; the refutation of Newton that would <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2015/05/07/rebecca-goldstein-incompleteness-godel-einstein-time/\">rattle the flow of existence</a>, forever changing our understanding of time; rather, Einstein was thinking of time as a plaything of mathematics, the cold clay of an impartial universe in which we ourselves are playthings of chance. </p>\n<p>Or was he? </p>\n<p>After all, a revolution in understanding time is a revolution in understanding ourselves as creatures of time, and no human being &#8212; not even the most abstract-minded physicist &#8212; can think about time without thinking about what it means to be human, to be concretely oneself, tender with transience. </p>\n<p>That is the predicate of the slender, poetic 1993 novel <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Einsteins-Dreams-Alan-Lightman/dp/140007780X/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><strong><em>Einstein&#8217;s Dreams</em></strong></a> (<a href=\"https://www.worldcat.org/title/einsteins-dreams/oclc/1041255372?referer=di&#038;ht=edition\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><em>public library</em></a>) by physicist <strong>Alan Lightman</strong> &#8212; a book about time and the tricks we play on ourselves to bear our transience, a book that does for time what Alain de Botton&#8217;s <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2016/08/15/alain-de-botton-the-course-of-love-communicator/\"><em>The Course of Love</em></a> does for love: punctuating a fictional world with philosophical quickenings, thought experiments, lyrical reflections on a fundamental human dimension of the real world. </p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/EinsteinsDreams_NotActuallyEinstein-1.jpg?resize=680%2C422&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"422\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-74274\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/EinsteinsDreams_NotActuallyEinstein-1.jpg?w=1849&#38;ssl=1 1849w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/EinsteinsDreams_NotActuallyEinstein-1.jpg?resize=320%2C199&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/EinsteinsDreams_NotActuallyEinstein-1.jpg?resize=600%2C373&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/EinsteinsDreams_NotActuallyEinstein-1.jpg?resize=240%2C149&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/EinsteinsDreams_NotActuallyEinstein-1.jpg?resize=768%2C477&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/EinsteinsDreams_NotActuallyEinstein-1.jpg?resize=1536%2C954&#38;ssl=1 1536w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/EinsteinsDreams_NotActuallyEinstein-1.jpg?w=1360&#38;ssl=1 1360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></p>\n<p>The young Einstein, overworked and burning with ideas, falls asleep at his patent office desk on a series of nights in that fertile spring of 1905, to dream of worlds in each of which times works differently. Each betokens a particular manifestation of our time-anxiety, that defining anxiety of our lives &#8212; each a particular tapestry of our hopes, fears, and other flights from the only reality we have and only place we really inhabit: the present. </p>\n<p>In one of these worlds, two times exist in parallel &#8212; mechanical time, &#8220;as rigid and metallic as a massive pendulum of iron that swings back and forth, back and forth, back and forth,&#8221; and body time, pulsating with aliveness that &#8220;squirms and wriggles like a bluefish in a bay.&#8221; This world is a testament to astronomer Maria Mitchell&#8217;s long-ago lament that <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2017/06/05/maria-mitchell-science-religion/\">&#8220;it seems to be difficult for any one to take in the idea that two truths cannot conflict&#8221;</a> &#8212; in it, people live out their lives subscribing to one time, distrusting and deriding the very existence of the other:</p>\n<blockquote><p>Where the two times meet, desperation. Where the two times go their separate ways, contentment. For, miraculously, a barrister, a nurse, a baker can make a world in either time, but not in both times. Each time is true, but the truths are not the same.</p></blockquote>\n<p>Another dream draws on the real history of <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2014/10/20/how-we-got-to-know-steven-johnson-hummingbird-effect-time/\">how Galileo invented timekeeping</a> to paint a world in which people journey to the Temple of Time to worship the Great Clock enshrined in it &#8212; a world part-prophecy and part-admonition, caricaturing our modern cult of the clock as humanity&#8217;s great concession in letting time reign, in <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2017/02/21/nina-simone-time/\">Nina Simone&#8217;s soulful words</a>, as &#8220;the great dictator.&#8221; Lightman writes:</p>\n<blockquote><p>Long ago, before the Great Clock, time was measured by changes in heavenly bodies: the slow sweep of stars across the night sky, the arc of the sun and variation in light, the waxing and waning of the moon, tides, seasons. Time was measured also by heartbeats, the rhythms of drowsiness and sleep, the recurrence of hunger, the menstrual cycles of women, the duration of loneliness. Then, in a small town in Italy, the first mechanical clock was built. People were spellbound. Later they were horrified. Here was a human invention that quantified the passage of time, that laid ruler and compass to the span of desire, that measured out exactly the moments of a life. It was magical, it was unbearable, it was outside natural law. Yet the clock could not be ignored. It would have to be worshipped. The inventor was persuaded to build the Great Clock. Afterwards, he was killed and all other clocks were destroyed. Then the pilgrimages began.</p></blockquote>\n<figure id=\"attachment_68203\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/temple-of-time-by-emma-willard-1846_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/07/templeoftime_willard1.jpg?resize=680%2C486&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"486\" class=\"size-full wp-image-68203\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/07/templeoftime_willard1.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/07/templeoftime_willard1.jpg?resize=240%2C171&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/07/templeoftime_willard1.jpg?resize=320%2C229&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/07/templeoftime_willard1.jpg?resize=768%2C548&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/07/templeoftime_willard1.jpg?resize=600%2C429&#38;ssl=1 600w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\"><em>Guide to the Temple of Time</em> by the visionary 19th-century cartographer and information designer <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2019/07/09/emma-willard/\">Emma Willard</a>. (Available <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/temple-of-time-by-emma-willard-1846_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a print</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>There is a world in which &#8220;time is a circle, bending back on itself&#8221; so that every instance, every event, every person &#8220;repeats itself, precisely, endlessly.&#8221;</p>\n<p>There is a world in which time comes with a pre-determined terminus, the precise date of which is known to all inhabitants, none of whom seem to mind that the world is ending, for &#8220;a world with one month is a world of equality.&#8221;</p>\n<p>There is a world in which entropy moves in reverse, everything tending from chaos to order, from dissolution to coherence &#8212; the shoreline rebuilt with each lapping wave, the house paint growing more vibrant with each passing season. </p>\n<p>There is a world located at the center of time, where time stands still, traveling outward in concentric circles to the outside worlds. Lovers and the parents of small children make pilgrimages to this place, hoping to preserve their fleeting bliss: </p>\n<blockquote><p>Some say it is best not to go near the center of time. Life is a vessel of sadness, but it is noble to live life, and without time there is no life. Others disagree. They would rather have an eternity of contentment, even if that eternity were fixed and frozen, like a butterfly mounted in a case.</p></blockquote>\n<p>There is a world in which imagining the future &#8212; that <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2014/07/01/mental-time-travel-dan-falk/\">capacity for mental time-travel essential for our humanity</a> &#8212; &#8220;is no more possible than seeing colors beyond violet,&#8221; and so every experience is absolute and eternal to those undergoing it:</p>\n<blockquote><p>In a world without future, each parting of friends is a death. In a world without future, each loneliness is final. In a world without future, each laugh is the last laugh. In a world without future, beyond the present lies nothingness, and people cling to the present as if hanging from a cliff.</p></blockquote>\n<p>Then there is the opposite world, in which the future is an omnipresent fixity:</p>\n<blockquote><p>This is a world in which time is not fluid, parting to make way for events. Instead, time is a rigid, bonelike structure, extending infinitely ahead and behind, fossilizing the future as well as the past. Every action, every thought, every breath of wind, every flight of birds is completely determined, forever&#8230; In a world of fixed future, life is an infinite corridor of rooms, one room lit at each moment, the next room dark but prepared. We walk from room to room, look into the room that is lit, the present moment, then walk on. We do not know the rooms ahead, but we know we cannot change them. We are spectators of our lives.</p></blockquote>\n<p>Then there is the opposite of the opposite, in which the past &#8212; that sole solidity of the real world &#8212; is unfixed, unvoided of possibility. In that world, a middle-aged man has spent his life trapped in a painful memory of childhood humiliation that has come to define his identity and behavior, until one day he wakes up to a different past, devoid of the event that produced the memory, and is suddenly a different person altogether. (Isn&#8217;t this the great dream of therapy, the great gift of healing &#8212; the dream of self-revision?) From this imaginary world, as from all the rest, Lightman wrests a reflection on the real world, lucid and lyrical:</p>\n<blockquote><p>What is the past? Could it be, the firmness of the past is just illusion? Could the past be a kaleidoscope, a pattern of images that shift with each disturbance of a sudden breeze, a laugh, a thought? And if the shift is everywhere, how would we know?</p>\n<p>[&#8230;]</p>\n<p>In a world of shifting past, these memories are wheat in wind, fleeting dreams, shapes in clouds. Events, once happened, lose reality, alter with a glance, a storm, a night. In time, the past never happened. But who could know? Who could know that the past is not as solid as this instant, when the sun streams over the Bernese Alps and the shopkeepers sing as they raise their awnings and the quarryman begins to load his truck.</p></blockquote>\n<figure  class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/vanish5800978_print?sku=s6-21581797p4a1v46?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2014/06/bridge_fog_new.jpg?resize=680%2C680&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"680\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-74229\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2014/06/bridge_fog_new.jpg?w=1936&#38;ssl=1 1936w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2014/06/bridge_fog_new.jpg?resize=320%2C320&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2014/06/bridge_fog_new.jpg?resize=600%2C600&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2014/06/bridge_fog_new.jpg?resize=240%2C240&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2014/06/bridge_fog_new.jpg?resize=768%2C768&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2014/06/bridge_fog_new.jpg?resize=1536%2C1536&#38;ssl=1 1536w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2014/06/bridge_fog_new.jpg?w=1360&#38;ssl=1 1360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\"><em>Vanish</em> by Maria Popova. (Available <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/vanish5800978_print?sku=s6-21581797p4a1v46?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a print</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Having spent half of my own life trapped in a self-created world of rigid routines and clockwork habits &#8212; a half-conscious effort to manufacture the illusion of constancy and continuity, to cope with the uncertainty and unpredictability of life, to deny the fact that to be human is to be inconstant and discontinuous ourselves &#8212; there is one world that particularly thrills me and particularly terrifies me:</p>\n<blockquote><p>In this world time is not continuous. In this world time is discontinuous. Time is a stretch of nerve fibers: seemingly continuous from a distance but disjointed close up, with microscopic gaps between fibers. Nervous action flows through one segment of time, abruptly stops, pauses, leaps through a vacuum, and resumes in the neighboring segment. So tiny are the disconnections in time that a single second would have to be magnified and dissected into one thousand parts and each of those parts into one thousand parts before a single missing part of time could be spotted. </p>\n<p>So tiny are the disconnections in time that the gaps between segments are practically imperceptible. After each restart of time, the new world looks just like the old. The positions and motions of clouds appear exactly the same, the trajectories of birds, the flow of conversations, thoughts.</p>\n<p>The segments of time fit together almost perfectly, but not quite perfectly. On occasion, very slight displacements occur. For example, on this Tuesday in Berne, a young man and a young woman, in their late twenties, stand beneath a street lamp on Gerberngasse. They met one month ago. He loves her desperately, but he has already been crushed by a woman who left him without warning, and he is frightened of love. He must be sure with this woman. He studies her face, pleads silently for her true feelings, searches for the smallest sign, the slightest movement of her brow, the vaguest reddening of her cheeks, the moistness of her eyes. </p>\n<p>In truth, she loves him back, but she cannot put her love in words. Instead, she smiles at him, unaware of his fear. As they stand beneath the street lamp, time stops and restarts. Afterwards, the tilt of their heads is precisely the same, the cycle of their heartbeats shows no alteration. But somewhere in the deep pools of the woman’s mind, a dim thought has appeared that was not there before. The young woman reaches for this new thought, into her unconscious, and as she does so a gossamer vacancy crosses her smile. This slight hesitation would be invisible to any but the closest scrutiny, yet the urgent young man has noticed it and taken it for his sign. He tells the young woman that he cannot see her again, returns to his small apartment on Zeughausgasse, decides to move to Zürich and work in his uncle’s bank. The young woman walks slowly home from the lamppost on Gerberngasse and wonders why the young man did not love her.</p></blockquote>\n<figure id=\"attachment_68575\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/light-distribution-on-soap-bubble-from-le-monde-physique-1882_print?sku=s6-11475521p4a1v1?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/08/4.jpg?resize=680%2C993&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"993\" class=\"size-full wp-image-68575\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/08/4.jpg?w=2197&#38;ssl=1 2197w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/08/4.jpg?resize=240%2C351&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/08/4.jpg?resize=320%2C467&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/08/4.jpg?resize=768%2C1122&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/08/4.jpg?resize=600%2C876&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/08/4.jpg?w=1360&#38;ssl=1 1360w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/08/4.jpg?w=2040&#38;ssl=1 2040w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Art from the 19th-century French physics textbook <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2019/08/20/amedee-guillemin-le-monde-physique/\"><em>Les monde physique</em></a>. (Available <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/light-distribution-on-soap-bubble-from-le-monde-physique-1882_print?sku=s6-11475521p4a1v1?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a print</a>, as <a href=\"https://society6.com/brainpicker/collection/vintage-science-cards?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">stationery cards</a>, and <a href=\"https://society6.com/brainpicker/collection/vintage-science-face-masks?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a face mask</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>This world might also be the incubus of Lightman&#8217;s uncommon insight into <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2018/03/27/alan-lightman-searching-for-stars-on-an-island-in-maine/\">our longing for absolutes in a relative world</a> and <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2021/06/13/alan-lightman-probable-impossibilities/\">what actually gives meaning to our temporal lives</a> &#8212; ideas contoured in <em>Einstein&#8217;s Dreams</em>, which he would shade in over the course of decades with his uncommon palette of physics and existential poetics. </p>\n<p>Take, for instance, the dream-world in which time does not flow but sticks, adhering each town to a particular point in history and each person to a particular point in life. There is no shared stream of present in this world &#8212; only islands of neighboring solitudes, each suspended in a different moment of a different past:</p>\n<blockquote><p>The tragedy of this world is that no one is happy, whether stuck in a time of pain or of joy. The tragedy of this world is that everyone is alone. For a life in the past cannot be shared with the present. Each person who gets stuck in time gets stuck alone.</p></blockquote>\n<p>This, indeed, is the silent refrain of the novel: the haunting reminder that however the past and the future might unfold and refold in the origami of even the most elaborate time-model, unless we live in the present, we are not living at all. I am reminded of Kafka: <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2016/04/18/conversations-with-kafka-taoism-truth/\">&#8220;Reality is never and nowhere more accessible than in the immediate moment of one’s own life. It’s only there that it can be won or lost.&#8221;</a> I am reminded of Kierkegaard a century before him: <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2017/04/18/kierkegaard-concept-of-anxiety-time/\">“The moment is not properly an atom of time but an atom of eternity. It is the first reflection of eternity in time, its first attempt, as it were, at stopping time.”</a> Above all, I am reminded of Gaston Bachelard, who reconciled Einstein and Bergson&#8217;s <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2015/12/09/the-physicist-and-the-philosopher-einstein-bergson-jimena-canales/\">historic debate about time</a> with a larger truth merging the scientific reality and the subjective human truth of time: <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2016/01/18/intuition-of-the-instant-gaston-bachelard/\">“If our heart were large enough to love life in all its detail, we would see that every instant is at once a giver and a plunderer.”</a></p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_55643\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/meteor-shower-by-tienne-lopold-trouvelot-1868-6iq_print?sku=s6-4686079p4a1v3?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/meteors1.jpg?resize=680%2C891&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"The November meteors, observed between midnight and 5 A.M. on  November 13-14, 1868\" width=\"680\" height=\"891\" class=\"size-full wp-image-55643\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/meteors1.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/meteors1.jpg?resize=240%2C315&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/meteors1.jpg?resize=320%2C419&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/meteors1.jpg?resize=768%2C1007&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/meteors1.jpg?resize=600%2C787&#38;ssl=1 600w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Meteors by <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2016/07/07/trouvelots-astronomical-drawings/\">Étienne Léopold Trouvelot</a>. (Available <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/meteor-shower-by-tienne-lopold-trouvelot-1868-6iq_print?sku=s6-4686079p4a1v3?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a print</a>, as <a href=\"https://society6.com/brainpicker/collection/vintage-science-cards?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">stationery cards</a>, and <a href=\"https://society6.com/brainpicker/collection/vintage-science-face-masks?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a face mask</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>This intimation is what <em>Einstein&#8217;s Dream</em> leaves lingering in the deliciously discomposed mind. In the last world, which the dreamt-up Einstein dreams up in the first week of summer, time is a flock of nightingales. People race to capture under bell jars, and mostly fail. Only children have the energy and speed to catch the birds, but children have no desire to catch them, for time is already moving too sluggishly for them, each summer month already an eternity. (Which of us can forget the vast spacetime of loneliness that slackens the hammock of childhood?) On those rare occasions when an adult captures a nightingale under their bell jar, they rejoice in the frozen moment, but only for a moment &#8212; eventually, they discover that life itself is a warm-blooded creature, pulsating with the flow of time:</p>\n<blockquote><p>They savor the precise placement of family and friends, the facial expressions, the trapped happiness over a prize or a birth or romance, the captured smell of cinnamon or white double violets. The catchers delight in the moment so frozen but soon discover that the nightingale expires, its clear, flutelike song diminishes to silence, the trapped moment grows withered and without life.</p></blockquote>\n<p>Like <em>The Little Prince</em>, <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Einsteins-Dreams-Alan-Lightman/dp/140007780X/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><strong><em>Einstein&#8217;s Dreams</em></strong></a> remains one of those endlessly rereadable classics, unfurling new splendors of insight and subtleties of feeling which each reading. Complement it with Kahlil Gibran on <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2020/01/05/kahlil-gibran-prophet-time/\">befriending time</a>, then revisit <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2020/05/25/beginning-of-time/\">the little loophole in the Big Bang</a> exploring when time really began. </p>\n<hr /><h3>donating = loving</h3><p class=\"flipboard-keep\">For 15 years, I have been spending hundreds of hours and thousands of dollars each month to keep <em>Brain Pickings</em> going. It has remained free and ad-free and alive thanks to patronage from readers. I have no staff, no interns, no assistant — a thoroughly one-woman labor of love that is also my life and my livelihood. 00:55:07","updatedTime":"2021-09-28 00:55:07","title":"Place, Personhood, and the Hippocampus: The Fascinating Science of Magnetism, Autonoeic Consciousness, and What Makes Us Who We Are","link":"https://www.brainpickings.org/?p=74452","description":"<h3>&#8220;Often the places we grow up in&#8230; influence how we perceive and conceptualize the world, give us metaphors to live by, and shape the purpose that drives us.&#8221;</h3>\n<hr>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Wayfinding-Science-Mystery-Humans-Navigate/dp/1250096960/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\"><img width=\"320\" height=\"495\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/wayfinding_oconnor.jpg?fit=320%2C495&#38;ssl=1\" class=\"cover alignright size-medium\" alt=\"Place, Personhood, and the Hippocampus: The Fascinating Science of Magnetism, Autonoeic Consciousness, and What Makes Us Who We Are\" loading=\"lazy\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/wayfinding_oconnor.jpg?w=1650&#38;ssl=1 1650w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/wayfinding_oconnor.jpg?resize=320%2C495&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/wayfinding_oconnor.jpg?resize=600%2C927&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/wayfinding_oconnor.jpg?resize=240%2C371&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/wayfinding_oconnor.jpg?resize=768%2C1187&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/wayfinding_oconnor.jpg?resize=994%2C1536&#38;ssl=1 994w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/wayfinding_oconnor.jpg?resize=1325%2C2048&#38;ssl=1 1325w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 320px) 100vw, 320px\" /></a></p><p>“Place and a mind may interpenetrate till the nature of both is altered,” the Scottish mountaineer and poet Nan Shepherd wrote in <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2018/03/19/the-living-mountain-nan-shepherd/\">her lyrical love letter</a> to her native Highlands, echoing an ancient intuition about how our formative physical landscapes shape our landscapes of thought and feeling. The word &#8220;genius&#8221; in the modern sense, after all, originates in the Latin phrase <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2019/10/01/what-miss-mitchell-saw/\"><em>genius loci</em></a> &#8212; &#8220;the spirit of a place.&#8221;</p>\n<p>I find myself thinking about Shepherd as I return to the Bulgarian mountains of my own childhood, trekking the same paths with my mother that I once trudged with tiny feet beside her, astonished at the flood of long-ago feelings rushing in with each step, astonished too at how effortlessly I navigate these routes I have not walked in decades.  </p>\n<p>The psychological, neurocognitive, and geophysical underpinnings of these astonishments are what <strong>M.R. O&#8217;Connor</strong> explores in <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Wayfinding-Science-Mystery-Humans-Navigate/dp/1250096960/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><strong><em>Wayfinding: The Science and Mystery of How Humans Navigate the World</em></strong></a> (<a href=\"https://www.worldcat.org/title/wayfinding-the-science-and-mystery-of-how-humans-navigate-the-world/oclc/1103152952&#038;referer=brief_results\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><em>public library</em></a>) &#8212; a layered inquiry into the science and cultural poetics of how we orient in space and selfhood, illuminating the stunning interpenetration of the two. </p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_74455\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/view-of-nature-in-ascending-regions-by-levi-walter-yaggy-1893_framed-print?sku=s6-21915630p21a12v52a13v57?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/yaggi_mountains_small.jpg?resize=680%2C460&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"460\" class=\"size-full wp-image-74455\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/yaggi_mountains_small.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/yaggi_mountains_small.jpg?resize=320%2C217&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/yaggi_mountains_small.jpg?resize=600%2C406&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/yaggi_mountains_small.jpg?resize=240%2C162&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/yaggi_mountains_small.jpg?resize=768%2C520&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">&#8220;View of Nature in Ascending Regions&#8221; by Levi Walter Yaggy from <em>Geographical Portfolio &#8212; Comprising Physical, Political, Geological, and Astronomical Geography</em>, 1893. (Available as <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/view-of-nature-in-ascending-regions-by-levi-walter-yaggy-1893_framed-print?sku=s6-21915630p21a12v52a13v57?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">a print</a>, as a <a href=\"https://society6.com/brainpicker/collection/vintage-science-face-masks?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">face mask</a>, and as <a href=\"https://society6.com/brainpicker/collection/vintage-science-cards?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">stationery cards</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>In a passage evocative of Rebecca Solnit&#8217;s memorable observation that <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2014/08/04/field-guide-to-getting-lost-rebecca-solnit\">&#8220;never to get lost is not to live,&#8221;</a> O&#8217;Connor takes the telescopic perspective of evolutionary time to consider the cognitive handicap beneath this existential gift:</p>\n<blockquote><p>Life on earth has created millions of Ulyssean species undertaking epic journeys at scales both large and small. Getting lost is a uniquely human problem. Many animals are incredible navigators, capable of undertaking journeys that far eclipse our individual abilities. The greatest migration on earth belongs to the Arctic tern, a four-ounce argonaut that travels each year from Greenland to Antarctica and back again, a distance of some forty-four thousand miles. Flying with the wind, the tern’s return itinerary is a globe-trotter’s fantasy, circumnavigating Africa and South America.</p>\n<p>[&#8230;]</p>\n<p>One of the devices that an animal needs to navigate is a “clock” &#8212; an internal mechanism for measuring or keeping time. The daily mass migration of zooplankton in the world’s oceans requires them to know when dawn and dusk are approaching. It would seem this is a simple response to light stimuli, but deep-sea zooplankton, which live at depths below where light penetrates, also migrate in accordance with the length of day at different latitudes. Even slightly more complex migrations can demand multiple clocks.</p></blockquote>\n<p>Perhaps the most astonishing internal clock belongs to the bioluminescent Bermuda fireworm, which swarms the tropical waters precisely fifty-seven minutes after sunset on each third evening after the full Moon in the summer. Such a feat suggests that this tiny marine organism, with a fraction of a fraction of the cognitive capacity of a human, is internally equipped with three different timekeeping devises: a regular twenty-four-hour diurnal clock, a lunar clock with a 27.3-day cycle, and an interval timer to tick out the exact minutes past sunset. </p>\n<figure  class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/discus-chronologicus-german-time-model-from-the-1720s_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/07/DiscusChronologicus_small.jpg?resize=680%2C728&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"728\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-74249\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/07/DiscusChronologicus_small.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/07/DiscusChronologicus_small.jpg?resize=320%2C342&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/07/DiscusChronologicus_small.jpg?resize=600%2C642&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/07/DiscusChronologicus_small.jpg?resize=240%2C257&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/07/DiscusChronologicus_small.jpg?resize=768%2C822&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\"><em>Discus chronologicus</em> &#8212; a German depiction of time from the early 1720s, included in <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2012/02/07/cartographies-of-time/\"><em>Cartographies of Time</em></a>. (Available as <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/discus-chronologicus-german-time-model-from-the-1720s_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">a print</a> and as <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/discus-chronologicus-german-time-model-from-the-1720s_wall-clock?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">a wall clock</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>O&#8217;Connor marvels at the staggering evolutionary array of timekeeping devices that allows migratory species to keep partaking of the dance of life:</p>\n<blockquote><p>Animals that complete annual migrations or multiyear migrations have to possess a yearly clock, one that is finely attuned to the lengths of days and nights and their changes across each season. In all, evolution seems to have produced annual clocks, lunar clocks, tidal clocks, circadian clocks, and, perhaps for those that migrate under cover of darkness, a sidereal clock &#8212; which measures the time it takes a star to appear to travel around the earth.</p></blockquote>\n<p>Besides their intricate internal timekeeping mechanisms, many nonhuman animals are endowed with equally intricate space-mapping mechanisms. Each migration season, humpback whales travel more than ten thousand miles far from land to return to the precise place where they were born. There are bird species &#8212; European pied flycatchers, blackcaps, and indigo buntings among them &#8212; that appear to orient by the pole star in their nocturnal flight; there are insect species &#8212; ants and bees among them &#8212; that perform triumphs of trigonometry with their light-sensitive photoreceptors, calculating spatial distances by polarized light to find the most direct route home after a winding pathway of foraging. With their mere milligram-brains of one million neurons &#8212; a grain of sand to the Mont Blanc of our eighty-six billion &#8212; and 20/2000 vision that renders them blind by human standards, honeybees make hundreds of foraging trips per day, meandering many miles from home, then compute the &#8220;beeline&#8221; back. African ball-rolling dung beetles, Namibian desert spiders, and southern cricket frogs use the stars of the Milky Way as their compass, just like some of the most courageous members of our own species once used the constellations to find their way to freedom from the moral cowardice of tyranny: To ensure they were moving northward, migrants on the Underground Railroad were instructed to keep the river on one side and &#8220;follow The Drinking Gourd&#8221; &#8212; an African name for Ursa Major, or The Big Dipper. </p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_74455\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/planetary-system-eclipse-of-the-sun-the-moon-the-zodiacal-light-meteoric-shower-by-levi-walter-yaggi-1887_framed-print?sku=s6-21917341p21a12v52a13v57?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/yaggi_astronomical_small.jpg?resize=680%2C452&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"452\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-74462\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/yaggi_astronomical_small.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/yaggi_astronomical_small.jpg?resize=320%2C213&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/yaggi_astronomical_small.jpg?resize=600%2C399&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/yaggi_astronomical_small.jpg?resize=240%2C160&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/yaggi_astronomical_small.jpg?resize=768%2C511&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">&#8220;Planetary System, Eclipse of the Sun, the Moon, the Zodiacal Light, Meteoric Shower&#8221; by Levi Walter Yaggy from <em>Geographical Portfolio &#8212; Comprising Physical, Political, Geological, and Astronomical Geography</em>, 1887. (Available as <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/planetary-system-eclipse-of-the-sun-the-moon-the-zodiacal-light-meteoric-shower-by-levi-walter-yaggi-1887_framed-print?sku=s6-21917341p21a12v52a13v57?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">a print</a>, as a <a href=\"https://society6.com/brainpicker/collection/vintage-science-face-masks?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">face mask</a>, and as <a href=\"https://society6.com/brainpicker/collection/vintage-science-cards?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">stationery cards</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Like all reality-radicalizing discoveries that defy the limiting creaturely intuitions we call common sense, the notion that animals might use magnetism for navigation was long derided as something more akin to spiritualism than to science. Humphry Davy &#8212; the greatest chemist of the Golden Age of chemistry, charismatic pioneer of the scientific lecture as popular entertainment &#8212; was keenly interested in the mystery of animal magnetism. A century after him, Nikola Tesla &#8212; a dazzling mind <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2015/07/10/nikola-tesla-when-woman-is-boss/\">epochs ahead of his time</a> in myriad ways, whose legacy shapes so much of our daily lives and whose name is now the measuring unit of magnetic fields &#8212; stood a chance of cracking the mystery, given with his twin passions for pigeons and magnetism, but the opprobrium of the scientific establishment was too impenetrable and the technology was not yet there. It wasn&#8217;t until 1958 that a young German graduate student &#8212; Wolfgang Wiltschko &#8212; was tasked with disproving animal magnetic navigation once and for all. Instead, he ended up proving it: In the then-dubious experiment he was asked to replicate, the birds he let loose in a space with no light source could, just like in the original experiment performed by a fellow student, still orient effortlessly. </p>\n<p>O&#8217;Connor writes:</p>\n<blockquote><p>The notion that animals have a bio-compass that can “read” the earth’s geomagnetic field has now emerged as the most promising explanation of animal navigation. In addition to those marathon migratory species, nearly every animal that has been tested thus far demonstrates a capacity to orient to the geomagnetic field. Carp floating in tubs at fish markets in Prague spontaneously align themselves in a north-south axis. So do newts at rest, and dogs when they crouch to relieve themselves. Horses, cattle, and deer orient their bodies north-south while grazing, but not if they are under power lines, which disrupt the magnetic field. Red foxes almost always pounce on mice from the northeast. These organisms must all have some kind of organelle that functions as a magneto-receptor, the same way an ear receives sound and an eye receives space.</p></blockquote>\n<figure  class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2012/12/03/berenice-abbott-documenting-science/\"><img src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2012/12/bereniceabbott_documentingscience8.jpg?w=680&#038;ssl=1\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\"><em>Magnetism with Key</em> by Berenice Abbott, 1958, from her series <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2012/12/03/berenice-abbott-documenting-science/\"><em>Documenting Science</em></a>.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>We human animals navigate the world not only by orienting in space, but by orienting in time. Mental time travel &#8212; the ability to rememeber and reflect, to imagine and plan for the future &#8212; is <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2014/07/01/mental-time-travel-dan-falk/\">what made us human</a>. It is also <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2018/01/15/oliver-sacks-identity-self-narrative/\">the pillar of our personal identity</a> &#8212; the narrative string that links our childhood selves to our present selves to make us, across a lifetime of physical and psychological changes, <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2014/10/07/rebecca-goldstein-personal-identity/\">one person</a>. </p>\n<p>That string is known as <em>autonoeic consciousness</em>, from the Greek <em>noéō</em>: &#8220;I perceive,&#8221; &#8220;I fathom&#8221; &#8212; our capacity for mental self-representation as entities in time that can reflect on our own lives as continuous and coherent phenomena of being. In the blink of evolutionary time since <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2017/02/23/beautiful-brain-santiago-ramon-y-cajal/\">the dawn of neuroscience</a> in the 1930s, one area of the brain has emerged as the crucible of both our autoneoic consciousness and our spatial navigation: the hippocampus. O&#8217;Connor writes:</p>\n<blockquote><p>The hippocampus has sometimes been described as the human GPS, but this metaphor is reductive compared to what this remarkable, plastic part of our minds accomplishes. While a GPS identifies fixed positions or coordinates in space that never change, neuroscientists think what the hippocampus does is unique to us as individuals &#8212; it builds representations of places based on our point of view, experiences, memories, goals, and desires. It provides the infrastructure for our selfhood.</p></blockquote>\n<figure id=\"attachment_60071\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2017/02/23/beautiful-brain-santiago-ramon-y-cajal/\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/02/BeautifulBrain_p072.jpg?resize=680%2C653&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"653\" class=\"size-full wp-image-60071\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/02/BeautifulBrain_p072.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/02/BeautifulBrain_p072.jpg?resize=240%2C230&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/02/BeautifulBrain_p072.jpg?resize=320%2C307&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/02/BeautifulBrain_p072.jpg?resize=768%2C737&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/02/BeautifulBrain_p072.jpg?resize=600%2C576&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/02/BeautifulBrain_p072.jpg?resize=32%2C32&#38;ssl=1 32w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">An astrocyte in the human hippocampus. One of neuroscience founding father Santiago Ramón y Cajal&#8217;s <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2017/02/23/beautiful-brain-santiago-ramon-y-cajal/\">little-known ink drawings</a>.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Because a self is a pattern of experiences, memories, and impressions, constellated according to an organizing principle, and because sleep is when the hippocampus consolidates memories to draw from them those organizing patterns, sleep is essential to our sense of self. O&#8217;Connor quotes MIT neuroscientist Matt Wilson: </p>\n<blockquote><p>During sleep you try to make sense of things you already learned&#8230; You go into a vast database of experience and try to figure out new connections and then build a model to explain new experiences. Wisdom is the rules, based on experience, that allows us to make good decisions in novel situations in the future.</p></blockquote>\n<p>The hippocampus is a hard-won glory of evolution, but it is not singular to us &#8212; rudiments of it and variations on it are found in some of our fellow animals across the rungs of neural complexity:</p>\n<blockquote><p>Even birds, which last shared an ancestor with humans 250 million years ago, as well as amphibians, lungfish, and reptiles, have what is called a medial pallium. Similar to the mammalian hippocampal formation in vertebrates, the medial pallium is also involved in spatial tasks in these species, raising the possibility that certain properties of spatial cognition were conserved as organisms diversified and split, while other properties adapted to particular ecologies or selective forces. But despite the profound evolutionary commonalities between humans and other vertebrates and the way the hippocampus relates to cognitive functions of memory and navigation, the question remains: why did we make such a leap in terms of hippocampi’s size and role in our lives? Or as psychologist Daniel Casasanto puts it, “How did foragers become physicists in the eye blink of evolutionary time?”</p></blockquote>\n<p>Part of the answer might lie in the remarkable plasticity of the hippocampus. After the now-iconic 2000 study of the brains of London taxi drivers &#8212; which found that their elaborate qualification exam, requiring the memorization of thousands of city landmarks and 25,000 streets, resulted in significant increase in synapses and gray matter in the hippocampus &#8212; scientists have been studying what we can do to protect and even bolster our primary instrument for navigating space and selfhood. </p>\n<p>O&#8217;Connor points to the work of McGill University neuroscientist Véronique Bohbot, who has devised a hippocampal health regimen of recollection and navigation exercises of incrementally increasing difficulty that deliver marked structural growth of gray matter. <a href=\"https://www.neuronautilus.com\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">VeboLife</a> &#8212; the neurocognitive fitness training program she has devised &#8212; teaches people to navigate the familiar environment in deliberately novel ways, challenging trainees to reconfigure their default routes by taking new paths that require them to attend to new details and make new mental maps in the process. </p>\n<p>Optimal hippocampal health appears to be &#8212; like the optimal experience of life itself &#8212; a matter of paying active and mindful attention, interrupting the <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2013/08/12/on-looking-eleven-walks-with-expert-eyes/\">&#8220;intentional, unapologetic discriminator&#8221;</a> our brain has evolved to be, savoring the specifics of each unrepeatable moment. </p>\n<p><iframe loading=\"lazy\" title=\"Studio Brussel: Joan As Police Woman - Kiss The Specifics\" width=\"680\" height=\"383\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/41kH-Ezu3B0?start=103&#038;feature=oembed\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe></p>\n<p>With an eye to how our hippocampal acuity determines the quality of our lives, O&#8217;Connor wonders:</p>\n<blockquote><p>Maybe wayfinding is an activity that confronts us with the marvelous fact of being in the world, requiring us to look up and take notice, to cognitively and emotionally interact with our surroundings whether we are in the wilderness or a city, even calling us to renew our species’ love affair with freedom, exploration, and place.</p></blockquote>\n<p>And yet as much as we throb with wanderlust, we are animated by an intense connection to the landscapes and topographies of our formative years. An emotion known as <em>topophilia</em>, which I experienced while revisiting those mountain trails of my childhood, furnishes this affective-spatial memory that renders childhood as much a time as a place.</p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_74456\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/rivers-and-mountains-of-the-world-1829_framed-print?sku=s6-21915678p21a12v52a13v57?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/mountainsandriversoftheworldjpg.jpg?resize=680%2C488&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"488\" class=\"size-full wp-image-74456\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/mountainsandriversoftheworldjpg.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/mountainsandriversoftheworldjpg.jpg?resize=320%2C230&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/mountainsandriversoftheworldjpg.jpg?resize=600%2C431&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/mountainsandriversoftheworldjpg.jpg?resize=240%2C172&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/mountainsandriversoftheworldjpg.jpg?resize=768%2C551&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Major rivers and mountains of the world compared by length and height, from <em>Atlas de Choix, ou Recueil des Meilleures Cartes de Geographie Ancienne et Moderne Dressees par Divers Auteurs</em> by J. Goujon and J. Andriveau, 1829. (Available as <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/rivers-and-mountains-of-the-world-1829_framed-print?sku=s6-21915678p21a12v52a13v57?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">a print</a>, as a <a href=\"https://society6.com/brainpicker/collection/vintage-science-face-masks?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">face mask</a>, and as <a href=\"https://society6.com/brainpicker/collection/vintage-science-cards?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">stationery cards</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>O&#8217;Connor writes:</p>\n<blockquote><p>Often the places we grow up in have outsized influence on us. They influence how we perceive and conceptualize the world, give us metaphors to live by, and shape the purpose that drives us &#8212; they are our source of subjectivity as well as a commonality by which we can relate to and identify with others. Maybe it’s because of the vividness of their sensory impressions, their genius for establishing deep relationships to their early environments, that children have a strong capacity for the human emotion called <em>topophilia</em>.</p>\n<p>[&#8230;]</p>\n<p>Across cultures, navigation is influenced by particular environmental conditions &#8212; snow, sand, water, wind &#8212; and topographies &#8212; mountain, valley, river, ocean, and desert. But in all of them, it is also a means by which individuals develop a sense of attachment and feeling for places. Navigating becomes a way of knowing, familiarity, and fondness. It is how you can fall in love with a mountain or a forest. Wayfinding is how we accumulate treasure maps of exquisite memories.</p></blockquote>\n<p>In the remainder of the thoroughly fascinating <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Wayfinding-Science-Mystery-Humans-Navigate/dp/1250096960/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><strong><em>Wayfinding</em></strong></a>, O&#8217;Connor maps the most thrilling shorelines of our evolving territories of understanding: astounding findings indicating that people from migratory populations have measurably longer alleles of the dopamine receptor gene associated with exploratory behavior than people from sedentary communities; ancient feats of navigation passed down the generations in native cultures to challenge the Western social theory of culture; music as a metaphor for the relationship between organisms and their environment. For a lyrical counterpart, complement it with Rebecca Solnit&#8217;s <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2014/08/04/field-guide-to-getting-lost-rebecca-solnit/\"><em>Field Guide to Getting Lost</em></a>.</p>\n<hr /><h3>donating = loving</h3><p class=\"flipboard-keep\">For 15 years, I have been spending hundreds of hours and thousands of dollars each month to keep <em>Brain Pickings</em> going. It has remained free and ad-free and alive thanks to patronage from readers. I have no staff, no interns, no assistant — a thoroughly one-woman labor of love that is also my life and my livelihood. If this labor makes your life more livable in any way, please consider aiding its sustenance with <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/donate/\">donation</a>.</p>\n\n<hr />\n\n<h3>newsletter</h3>\n<p>Brain Pickings has a free weekly newsletter.
