00:55:07","updatedTime":"2021-09-28 00:55:07","title":"Mary’s Room: An Animated Inquiry into the Limits of Knowledge and the Mystery of Consciousness","link":"https://www.brainpickings.org/?p=74192","description":"<h3>The gasp beyond fact, contouring the central question of what it is like to be you.</h3>\n<hr>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Theres-Something-About-Mary-Press/dp/0262621894?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\"><img width=\"320\" height=\"485\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/somethingaboutmary.jpg?fit=320%2C485&#38;ssl=1\" class=\"cover with-border alignright size-medium\" alt=\"Mary&#8217;s Room: An Animated Inquiry into the Limits of Knowledge and the Mystery of Consciousness\" loading=\"lazy\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/somethingaboutmary.jpg?w=324&#38;ssl=1 324w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/somethingaboutmary.jpg?resize=320%2C485&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/somethingaboutmary.jpg?resize=240%2C364&#38;ssl=1 240w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 320px) 100vw, 320px\" /></a></p><p>&#8220;It is not half so important to <em>know</em> as to <em>feel</em>,&#8221; Rachel Carson <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2013/12/23/rachel-carson-on-wonder/\">wrote</a> after catalyzing the environmental movement with the rigorous science and passionate poetics of reality, harmonizing fact with feeling as the score to a larger understanding. The sentiment speaks to something essential about our human experience: that understanding is always governed by feeling and that any factual knowledge, rather than shaping subjective experience, is shaped by it. </p>\n<p>Consciousness &#8212; that synaptic cataclysm of cerebration symphonic with feeling &#8212; is our only lens on reality, half-opaque to itself, its nature ever quickening our hardest questions, their answers ever beyond our grasp.   </p>\n<p>A decade after the electricity of life and subjective experience ceased firing in Carson&#8217;s consciousness, Hannah Arendt delivered her staggering Gifford Lectures on <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2014/09/16/hannah-arendt-the-life-of-the-mind/\">the life of the mind</a>, observing that if we ever relinquish our hunger for unanswerable questions &#8212; the pinnacle of &#8220;the appetite for meaning we call thinking&#8221; &#8212; we would not only lose all art, but lose science and &#8220;the capacity to ask all the answerable questions upon which every civilization is founded.&#8221; </p>\n<p>At the center of this delicious realm of the unanswerable are our <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2017/05/25/christof-koch-consciousness-qualia/\">qualia</a> &#8212; those subjective states springing from the essence of individual consciousness, intimate and inchoate, pulsating with the mystery of what it is like to be oneself: what it is like for you to look at the <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2018/05/17/two-hundred-years-of-blue/\">blue</a> I am looking at and see it in a way I never will, nor will ever grasp through knowledge. </p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_73608\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/blues-by-patrick-syme-from-werners-nomenclature-of-colours-1821_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2018/02/werner_blues-1.jpg?resize=680%2C1080&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"1080\" class=\"size-full wp-image-73608\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2018/02/werner_blues-1.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2018/02/werner_blues-1.jpg?resize=320%2C508&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2018/02/werner_blues-1.jpg?resize=600%2C953&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2018/02/werner_blues-1.jpg?resize=240%2C381&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2018/02/werner_blues-1.jpg?resize=768%2C1220&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2018/02/werner_blues-1.jpg?resize=967%2C1536&#38;ssl=1 967w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Color chart by Patrick Syme for <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2018/02/06/werner-nomenclature-of-colours/\"><em>Werner’s Nomenclature of Colours: Adapted to Zoology, Botany, Chemistry, Mineralogy, Anatomy, and the Arts</em></a>. (Available as <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/blues-by-patrick-syme-from-werners-nomenclature-of-colours-1821_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">a print</a> and as <a href=\"https://society6.com/brainpicker/collection/vintage-science-face-masks\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">stationery cards</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>In the early 1980s, the Australian philosopher <strong>Frank Jackson</strong> (b. August 31, 1943) set out to explore how knowable that mystery is with his <em>knowledge argument</em> &#8212; a thought experiment, also known as <em>Mary&#8217;s Room</em> or <em>Mary the Super-scientist</em>, probing the unfathomed regions of consciousness and the limits of what is knowable with the proboscis of our rational inquiry.</p>\n<p>Living in a black-and-white room, reading black-and-white books, and watching black-and-white screens, Jackson&#8217;s conceptual Mary studies what the world is and how it works &#8212; its physical structures, processes, and causal relationships. But then she leaves her monochrome confines and encounters color &#8212; itself the product of physical processes and phenomena, yet producing in Mary a perceptual-psychological experience beyond the knowledge of those processes and phenomena, beyond everything she had understood about color through the knowledge-acquisition paradigm of learning. </p>\n<p>A gasp beyond fact, intimating that knowledge of the physical might fail to capture some essential aspects of our consciousness, the experience of color being but one. An almost-answer to the ancient question Plato posed with his <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2015/03/23/plato-allegory-of-the-cave-ted-ed/\">thought experiment about consciousness and the nature of reality</a>, the question quantum theory originator Max Planck picked up two and half millennia later with his insistence that <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2019/06/12/max-planck-where-is-science-going/\">&#8220;science cannot solve the ultimate mystery of nature&#8230; because&#8230; we ourselves are part of nature and therefore part of the mystery that we are trying to solve.&#8221;</a></p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_72737\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/art-from-thomas-wrights-an-original-theory-or-new-hypothesis-of-the-universe-1750_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/thomaswright_galaxies3.jpg?resize=680%2C977&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"977\" class=\"size-full wp-image-72737\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/thomaswright_galaxies3.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/thomaswright_galaxies3.jpg?resize=240%2C345&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/thomaswright_galaxies3.jpg?resize=320%2C460&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/thomaswright_galaxies3.jpg?resize=768%2C1103&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/thomaswright_galaxies3.jpg?resize=600%2C862&#38;ssl=1 600w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Art from Thomas Wright&#8217;s <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2021/02/16/thomas-wright-original-theory/\"><em>An Original Theory or New Hypothesis of the Universe</em></a>, 1750. (Available as <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/art-from-thomas-wrights-an-original-theory-or-new-hypothesis-of-the-universe-1750_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">a print</a> and as <a href=\"https://society6.com/brainpicker/collection/vintage-science-face-masks?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">a face mask</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Originally devised as an argument against physicalism &#8212; the notion that everything known and knowable to us, through thought or feeling, has a physical fundament &#8212; the knowledge argument is widely considered <a href=\"https://amazon.com/Theres-Something-About-Mary-Press/dp/0262621894/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">&#8220;one of the most discussed, important, and controversial&#8221;</a> arguments in the <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2021/08/17/annaka-harris-conscious/\">ongoing quest to fathom consciousness</a>. That it was later challenged by Jackson himself suggests that we might, after all, be <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2021/06/13/alan-lightman-probable-impossibilities/\">stardust suspended in the hammock of spacetime</a>. </p>\n<p>This animated primer from my friends at <a href=\"https://ed.ted.com\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">TED-Ed</a> and chemist Eleanor Nelsen delves into the complexities, the revelations, and the unanswered, possibly unanswerable questions the knowledge argument contours &#8212; the central questions of what it is like to be human:</p>\n<p><iframe loading=\"lazy\" title=\"Mary&#039;s Room: A philosophical thought experiment - Eleanor Nelsen\" width=\"680\" height=\"383\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/mGYmiQkah4o?feature=oembed&#38;rel=0&#38;controls=0&#38;showinfo=0&#38;iv_load_policy=3\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe></p>\n<p>Complement with Richard Feynman&#8217;s <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2013/01/01/ode-to-a-flower-richard-feynman/\"><em>Ode to a Flower</em></a> &#8212; a Nobel-winning physicist&#8217;s sidewise gleam on the same abiding question &#8212; then consider a supreme counterpoint to physicalism in <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2021/08/21/clemency-burton-hill-pablo-casals-albert-schweitzer-bach/\">the mysterious experience of music</a>.</p>\n<hr /><h3>donating = loving</h3><p class=\"flipboard-keep\">For 15 years, I have been spending hundreds of hours and thousands of dollars each month to keep <em>Brain Pickings</em> going. It has remained free and ad-free and alive thanks to patronage from readers. I have no staff, no interns, no assistant — a thoroughly one-woman labor of love that is also my life and my livelihood. If this labor makes your life more livable in any way, please consider aiding its sustenance with <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/donate/\">donation</a>.</p>\n\n<hr />\n\n<h3>newsletter</h3>\n<p>Brain Pickings has a free weekly newsletter. Like? <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/newsletter/\">Sign up.</a></p><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/brainpickings/rss/~4/dikfJMr7RnQ\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Tue, 24 Aug 2021 16:00:14 +0000","feedId":17,"bgimg":"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/somethingaboutmary.jpg?fit=320%2C485&ssl=1","linkMd5":"e48aa7a6ff56d1b10c1a0078bc54ee55","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn28@2020_1/2021/09/27/16-55-08-908_e39cba9cfae8626b.webp","destWidth":320,"destHeight":485,"sourceBytes":14846,"destBytes":14846,"author":"Maria Popova","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/somethingaboutmary.jpg?fit=320%2C485&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn28@2020_1/2021/09/27/16-55-08-908_e39cba9cfae8626b.webp","https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2018/02/werner_blues-1.jpg?resize=680%2C1080&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn44@2020_4/2021/09/27/16-55-33-923_a20e25802328ace5.webp","https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/thomaswright_galaxies3.jpg?resize=680%2C977&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx31/cdn80@2020_6/2021/09/27/16-55-33-620_fc7479656e42f0a0.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/brainpickings/rss/~4/dikfJMr7RnQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn79@2020_5/2021/09/27/16-55-34-588_b2dbe2fca47527b7.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1632761707368},{"createdTime":"2021-09-28 00:55:06","updatedTime":"2021-09-28 00:55:06","title":"The Unfinished Story of the World: Richard Powers’s Advice on Life and the Antidote to Cynicism","link":"https://www.brainpickings.org/?p=74371","description":"<h3>&#8220;This fluke, single, huge, cross-indexed, thermodynamic experiment of a story that the world has been inventing to tell itself at bedtime is still in embryo. It&#8217;s not even the outline of a synopsis of notes toward a rough draft yet.&#8221;</h3>\n<hr>\n<p><a href=\"http://www.amazon.com/Take-My-Advice-Letters-Generation/dp/1416578358/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\"><img width=\"320\" height=\"495\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/takemyadvice_harmon.jpg?fit=320%2C495&#38;ssl=1\" class=\"cover alignright size-medium\" alt=\"The Unfinished Story of the World: Richard Powers&#8217;s Advice on Life and the Antidote to Cynicism\" loading=\"lazy\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/takemyadvice_harmon.jpg?w=880&#38;ssl=1 880w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/takemyadvice_harmon.jpg?resize=320%2C495&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/takemyadvice_harmon.jpg?resize=600%2C927&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/takemyadvice_harmon.jpg?resize=240%2C371&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/takemyadvice_harmon.jpg?resize=768%2C1187&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 320px) 100vw, 320px\" /></a></p><p>Perhaps the gravest violence we can do to ourselves is to live out our lives believing the world to be a fixity handed down to us by the authorities of history and life to be a matter of taking immutable givens. Daring to believe otherwise &#8212; to believe that even our smallest purposeful action alters the monolith of reality in some subtle, meaningful way &#8212; is an act of courage and resistance, an act of immense vulnerability to the possibility of disappointment, vulnerability the commonest cowering from which is cynicism. </p>\n<p>James Baldwin knew this when he issued his lyrical and impassioned insistence that <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2020/05/21/nothing-is-fixed-james-baldwin-morley-music/\">&#8220;nothing is fixed, forever and forever and forever, it is not fixed,&#8221;</a> that <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2016/05/09/james-baldwin-freedom/\">&#8220;we made the world we’re living in and we have to make it over.&#8221;</a> </p>\n<p>Hannah Arendt knew this when she considered <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2017/05/17/hannah-arendt-human-condition-speech-action/\">how we invent ourselves and reinvent the world</a>, observing that “the smallest act in the most limited circumstances bears the seed of boundlessness, because one deed, and sometimes one word, suffices to change every constellation.”</p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_72916\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/art-by-dorothy-lathrop-for-down-adown-derry-by-walter-de-la-mare-19224642772_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/downadownderry_dorothylathrop17.jpg?resize=680%2C801&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"801\" class=\"size-full wp-image-72916\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/downadownderry_dorothylathrop17.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/downadownderry_dorothylathrop17.jpg?resize=320%2C377&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/downadownderry_dorothylathrop17.jpg?resize=600%2C707&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/downadownderry_dorothylathrop17.jpg?resize=240%2C283&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/downadownderry_dorothylathrop17.jpg?resize=768%2C905&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Art by <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2021/03/09/dorothy-lathrop-down-adown-derry/\">Dorothy Lathrop</a>, 1922. (Available <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/art-by-dorothy-lathrop-for-down-adown-derry-by-walter-de-la-mare-19224642772_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a print</a> and <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/art-by-dorothy-lathrop-for-down-adown-derry-by-walter-de-la-mare-19224642772_cards?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as stationery cards</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p><strong>Richard Powers</strong> knew this when he made his contribution to <a href=\"http://www.amazon.com/Take-My-Advice-Letters-Generation/dp/1416578358/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><strong><em>Take My Advice: Letters to the Next Generation from People Who Know a Thing or Two</em></strong></a> (<a href=\"http://www.worldcat.org/title/take-my-advice-letters-to-the-next-generation-from-people-who-know-a-thing-or-two/oclc/49322746&#038;referer=brief_results\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><em>public library</em></a>) &#8212; artist and writer James L. Harmon&#8217;s wonderful 2002 anthology of <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2012/10/12/martha-nussbaum-take-my-advice/\">wisdom from stellar minds</a>, a decade in the constellating, envisioned as an eclectic contemporary counterpart to Rilke&#8217;s timeless <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2021/06/29/rilke-letters-to-a-young-poet-macy-barrows/\"><em>Letters to a Young Poet</em></a>, which had moved Harmon deeply when he first encountered it as a young man. </p>\n<p>Two decades before Powers won the Pulitzer Prize for his sylvan symphony <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Overstory-Novel-Richard-Powers/dp/039335668X/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><em>The Overstory</em></a>, he echoes Seamus Heaney&#8217;s exhortation to <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2016/01/19/seamus-heaney-commencement/\">always remain &#8220;true to your own secret knowledge&#8221;</a> and writes:</p>\n<blockquote><p>Never forget what you were born knowing. That this fluke, single, huge, cross-indexed, thermodynamic experiment of a story that the world has been inventing to tell itself at bedtime is still in embryo. It&#8217;s not even the outline of a synopsis of notes toward a rough draft yet. Buy the plot some time.</p></blockquote>\n<figure id=\"attachment_66441\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/solar-system-quilt-by-ellen-harding-baker-1886_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2018/12/ellenhardingbaker_solarsystemquilt1.jpg?resize=680%2C564&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"564\" class=\"size-full wp-image-66441\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2018/12/ellenhardingbaker_solarsystemquilt1.jpg?w=1000&#38;ssl=1 1000w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2018/12/ellenhardingbaker_solarsystemquilt1.jpg?resize=240%2C199&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2018/12/ellenhardingbaker_solarsystemquilt1.jpg?resize=320%2C266&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2018/12/ellenhardingbaker_solarsystemquilt1.jpg?resize=768%2C637&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2018/12/ellenhardingbaker_solarsystemquilt1.jpg?resize=600%2C498&#38;ssl=1 600w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">19th-century <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2018/12/06/ellen-harding-baker-solar-system-quilt/\">Solar System quilt</a> by Ellen Harding Baker, embroidered over the course of seven years as a teaching tool in an era when women were barred from higher education in science and a fraction of the presently known Solar System objects were known. (Available as <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/solar-system-quilt-by-ellen-harding-baker-1886_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">a print</a> and <a href=\"https://society6.com/brainpicker/collection/vintage-science-face-masks\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">a face mask</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>We buy the plot time with the currency of our conscious choices, the grand and the mundane alike &#8212; the daily actions that make us what we are, the people who make the world what it is. Powers writes:</p>\n<blockquote><p>Take in more, consume less, recycle everything; book-keep all hidden costs; find out where you have been set down; lobby for a smaller market; get rid of your car and travel as widely as you can (yeah, walk: what the hell); try to say a little more than you mean; carry a pocket encyclopedia (ask for one without packaging) and when the entry on &#8220;Diffusion Constant&#8221; says, &#8220;for more information, see &#8216;Pastry War,'&#8221; see &#8220;Pastry War.&#8221;</p></blockquote>\n<p>This latter sentiment might at first appear dated in the hindsight of two decades, in the epoch of Wikipedia. But it is actually all the more insightful and urgent today, for the quiet act of resistance at its heart has grown all the harder. What I most rue about the internet is that, for all its riches of readily accessible information, it has altered the texture of human curiosity, vanquishing that wondrous encyclopedic feeling of learning about the thing you hadn&#8217;t known you didn&#8217;t know but now greatly enjoy knowing. Somewhere along the way of choices being made for us by an insular tribe of technologists, discovery was sacrificed at the altar of search as algorithms perfected the mechanics of giving us more and more of what we already knew we wanted and believed, rendering the mind itself more and more a fixity. Would you be Googling &#8220;Pastry War&#8221; now had I not made this point about a point Richard Powers made long ago on the pages of a yellowing book I pulled from my bookshelf by some incomputable human impulse this morning? </p>\n<p>Those choices matter, Powers reminds us, even at the smallest scale. There is no fulcrum too small for the lever of change to lift from, but the lift must begin with lucidity. He writes:</p>\n<blockquote><p>Take a full look at the worst. Acknowledge the figures: the runaway birthdates, the irreversible extinctions and ruined habitats, the meaningless economies fueled by waste, the exported shooting wars and their cover causes&#8230; Then work at whatever comes to hand. Useful or not, it makes no difference. Jumping in is the only calculus that emergency ever allows.</p></blockquote>\n<p>Complement with Rebecca Solnit on <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2018/10/18/rebecca-solnit-call-them-by-their-true-names/\">rewriting the world&#8217;s broken stories with our actions</a>, then revisit <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2019/07/29/what-if-tallec-lenain/\"><em>What If</em></a> &#8212; a wondrous French picture-book about daring to imagine and build a different world for the children of tomorrow.</p>\n<hr /><h3>donating = loving</h3><p class=\"flipboard-keep\">For 15 years, I have been spending hundreds of hours and thousands of dollars each month to keep <em>Brain Pickings</em> going. It has remained free and ad-free and alive thanks to patronage from readers. I have no staff, no interns, no assistant — a thoroughly one-woman labor of love that is also my life and my livelihood. If this labor makes your life more livable in any way, please consider aiding its sustenance with <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/donate/\">donation</a>.</p>\n\n<hr />\n\n<h3>newsletter</h3>\n<p>Brain Pickings has a free weekly newsletter. https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/derekjarman_modernnature.jpg?resize=320%2C491&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/derekjarman_modernnature.jpg?resize=600%2C921&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/derekjarman_modernnature.jpg?resize=240%2C368&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/derekjarman_modernnature.jpg?resize=768%2C1179&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/derekjarman_modernnature.jpg?resize=1001%2C1536&#38;ssl=1 1001w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 320px) 100vw, 320px\" /></a></p><p>There is an elemental cosmic loneliness in the pit of every human soul. We spend our lives trying to make it bearable and call our efforts love, or art. (Which might, in the end, be one and the same.) Every once in a while, we are lifted out of the pit into a salutary sense of connection and congress with something larger &#8212; a sense of being but one wave among the incalculable lapping lonelinesses in the great sea of being, but one string in the grand symphony orchestra of aliveness. </p>\n<p>For many of us, this sense awakens most readily in the natural world, where we feel ourselves part of larger rhythms and larger scales beckoning us to take <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2017/12/21/reflection/\">the telescopic perspective</a> of time, space, and being with the broadened lens of the mind. Whitman felt it most intimately <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2020/12/16/on-the-beach-alone-at-night-walt-whitman/\">&#8220;on the beach alone at night.&#8221;</a> Hesse felt it <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2020/05/04/natascha-mcelhone-wander-hesse-kew/\">among the trees</a>. Antoine de Saint-Exupéry felt it <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2014/03/10/antoine-de-saint-exupery-letter-to-a-hostage-sahara/\">in the desert</a>. I feel it with my hand against the mosses carpeting the old-growth coastal forest. </p>\n<p>Many of humanity&#8217;s vastest, most sensitive-souled minds have turned to the natural world not only for creative fuel but for a <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2020/06/14/nature-depression/\">mighty antidote to melancholy</a>. Few have captured that ecstatic sense of cosmic belonging more exquisitely than the English artist and activist <strong>Derek Jarman</strong> (January 31, 1942&#8211;February 19, 1994) in <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Modern-Nature-Derek-Jarman/dp/178487387X/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><strong><em>Modern Nature</em></strong></a> (<a href=\"https://www.worldcat.org/title/modern-nature-the-journals-of-derek-jarman-1989-1990/oclc/1108243615&#038;referer=brief_results\" rel=\"noopener\"><em>public library</em></a>) &#8212; his almost unbearably beautiful record of leaving London to live in a former Victorian fisherman&#8217;s hut nestled between an old lighthouse and a nuclear power plant in a newly designated conservation area on the shingled shores of Kent. There, on this solitary headland, <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2021/04/04/derek-jarman-modern-nature-gardening/\">salving grief through gardening</a>, Jarman discovered the consolations of a different kind of time &#8212; not the time of atoms and anxieties, but the time of <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2020/03/18/figuring-shoreless-seeds-and-stardust/\">seeds and stars</a>. </p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_55649\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/the-milky-way-by-tienne-lopold-trouvelot-1874-1876-9hj_print#s6-4686059p4a1v45?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/milkyway1.jpg?resize=680%2C890&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"Part of the Milky Way, from a study made between 1874 and 1876\" width=\"680\" height=\"890\" class=\"size-full wp-image-55649\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/milkyway1.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/milkyway1.jpg?resize=240%2C314&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/milkyway1.jpg?resize=320%2C419&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/milkyway1.jpg?resize=768%2C1005&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/milkyway1.jpg?resize=600%2C786&#38;ssl=1 600w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">One of Étienne Léopold Trouvelot&#8217;s <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2016/07/07/trouvelots-astronomical-drawings/\">19th-century astronomical drawings</a>. (Available <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/the-milky-way-by-tienne-lopold-trouvelot-1874-1876-9hj_print#s6-4686059p4a1v45?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a print</a>, as <a href=\"https://society6.com/brainpicker/collection/vintage-science-cards?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">stationery cards</a>, and <a href=\"https://society6.com/brainpicker/collection/vintage-science-face-masks?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a face mask</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>One spring Saturday, after hanging five new paintings on his walls &#8212; &#8220;all collages of found objects on gold backgrounds&#8221; &#8212; Jarman writes in the journal:</p>\n<blockquote><p>A hallucinatory dusk, washed with colours to drive Monet to suicide. At sunset the brightest sickle moon appeared in a gentle blue sky; minute by minute gathering in intensity it stayed until just before midnight.</p>\n<p>Night clear as a bell &#8212; the blue passed through violet with strands of rose and old gold to become a deep indigo. So etched were the moon and stars they seemed to have been cut out by a child to decorate a crib.</p>\n<p>The night sky here is a riot that outshines the brightest lights of Piccadilly; the stars have the intensity of jewels. So flat is the Ness that those stars that lie at the horizon touch your very feet and the moon tips the waves with silver.</p></blockquote>\n<p>The passage reminds me of a breathtaking piece by my composer-friend <a href=\"https://www.jherekbischoff.com\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Jherek Bischoff</a> &#8212; a piece inspired by one particular night from his boyhood, living on a sailboat with his parents hundreds of miles from land, when the surface of the open ocean was so still that he could no longer discern the horizon line: the stars in the sky and their reflections in the water appeared as a single sphere of spacetime, inside which he felt to be floating.</p>\n<p><iframe loading=\"lazy\" title=\"The Sea&#039;s Son\" width=\"680\" height=\"510\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/nHlBpybApRs?feature=oembed&#38;rel=0&#38;controls=0&#38;showinfo=0&#38;iv_load_policy=3\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe></p>\n<p>From his starlit garden perch between the lighthouse and the power plant, Jarman suddenly sees the familiar landscape with new cosmic eyes, all radiance and rapture:</p>\n<blockquote><p>The nuclear power station is a great ocean liner moored in the firmament, ablaze with light: white, yellow, ruby. Whilst round the bay the lights stretch from Folkenstone to Dover. High above, jet liners from the south float silent in the stars. On these awesome nights, reduced to silence, I walk across the Ness.</p>\n<p>Never in my many sleepless nights have I witnessed a spectacle like this. Not the antique bells of the flocks moving up a Sardinian hillside, the barking of the dogs and the sharp cries of the shepherd boys, nor moonlit nights sailing the Aegean, nor the scented nights and fireflies of Fire Island, smashed glass star-strewn through the piers along the Hudson &#8212; nothing can quite equal this.</p></blockquote>\n<p>In consonance with his artistic and spiritual progenitor Walt Whitman&#8217;s faith in <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2017/11/17/walt-whitman-specimen-days-music/\">the indelible connection between music and nature</a> and with Joseph Cornell&#8217;s <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2020/11/24/joseph-cornell-planetarium/\">artistically formative experience at the planetarium</a>, Jarman adds:</p>\n<blockquote><p>The orchestra has struck up the music of the spheres, the spectral dancers on the fated liner whirl you off your feet till you feel the great globe move. Light-hearted laughter. Here man<a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2014/10/17/ursula-k-le-guin-gender/\">*</a> has invented the heavens&#8217; but the moon, not to be usurped, shines sickle bright, gathering our souls.</p></blockquote>\n<figure id=\"attachment_74295\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/derekjarman1.jpg?resize=680%2C832&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"832\" class=\"size-full wp-image-74295\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/derekjarman1.jpg?w=1000&#38;ssl=1 1000w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/derekjarman1.jpg?resize=320%2C391&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/derekjarman1.jpg?resize=600%2C734&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/derekjarman1.jpg?resize=240%2C294&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/derekjarman1.jpg?resize=768%2C939&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Derek Jarman</figcaption></figure>\n<p>In this passage from <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Modern-Nature-Derek-Jarman/dp/178487387X/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><strong><em>Modern Nature</em></strong></a>, Jarman does for the night sky what Rachel Carson did a generation earlier for <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2021/06/07/rachel-carson-the-edge-of-the-sea/\">the ocean as a lens on the meaning of life</a>. Complement it with the great nature writer Henry Beston &#8212; Carson&#8217;s great hero &#8212; on <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2015/06/04/henry-beston-night-outermost-house/\">night and the human spirit</a>, then revisit poet Marie Howe&#8217;s Whitman-inspired, Hawking-inspired <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2020/04/23/singularity-marie-howe-animated/\">ode to our cosmic belonging</a>.</p>\n<hr /><h3>donating = loving</h3><p class=\"flipboard-keep\">For 15 years, I have been spending hundreds of hours and thousands of dollars each month to keep <em>Brain Pickings</em> going. It has remained free and ad-free and alive thanks to patronage from readers. I have no staff, no interns, no assistant — a thoroughly one-woman labor of love that is also my life and my livelihood. Popova","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/derekjarman_modernnature.jpg?fit=320%2C491&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn39@2020_6/2021/09/27/16-55-07-621_4c306750f1b7a1f0.webp","https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/milkyway1.jpg?resize=680%2C890&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn8@2020_1/2021/09/27/16-55-33-848_47506297f6838c31.webp","https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/derekjarman1.jpg?resize=680%2C832&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx11/cdn90@2020_5/2021/09/27/16-55-33-253_1e9b12b37540a59d.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/brainpickings/rss/~4/AkOvwBy-LkY":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn24@2020_1/2021/09/27/16-55-33-455_240a8321c51b6aef.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1632761707369},{"createdTime":"2021-09-28 00:55:07","updatedTime":"2021-09-28 00:55:07","title":"Between Restlessness and Rapture: Autumn and the Sensual Urgency of Aliveness","link":"https://www.brainpickings.org/?p=74439","description":"<h3>A wildlife ecologist&#8217;s serenade to the season that makes you &#8220;want to linger long enough to hear every sound and look far enough to see into forever.&#8221;</h3>\n<hr>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Home-Place-Memoirs-Colored-Affair/dp/1571313508/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\"><img width=\"320\" height=\"495\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/lanham_thehomeplace.jpg?fit=320%2C495&#38;ssl=1\" class=\"cover alignright size-medium\" alt=\"Between Restlessness and Rapture: Autumn and the Sensual Urgency of Aliveness\" loading=\"lazy\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/lanham_thehomeplace.jpg?w=506&#38;ssl=1 506w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/lanham_thehomeplace.jpg?resize=320%2C495&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/lanham_thehomeplace.jpg?resize=240%2C371&#38;ssl=1 240w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 320px) 100vw, 320px\" /></a></p><p>When autumn comes with its ecstasy of sweetness in the orchard and its symphony of color in the forest, it staggers us with something difficult to name, some bewildering harmonic of the transcendent and the transient &#8212; each ripening apple an aria of delight, each bright falling leaf a sigh, a homily, a dirge without music. </p>\n<p>Looking back on her life in its final year, the great French writer, actor, and mime Colette celebrated autumn and the autumn of life as <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2016/09/22/colette-autumn/\">a beginning, not a decline</a> &#8212; the season of &#8220;those who have nothing more to lose and so excel at giving.&#8221; Two generations later, while navigating a season of bereavements, Pico Iyer discovered in autumn existential training ground for <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2019/10/11/autumn-light-pico-iyer/\">finding beauty in impermanence and light in loss</a>. We call it &#8220;fall,&#8221; but something swells in us as the days grow shorter and the trees more skeletal &#8212; the quiet uprising of resilience that readies us for <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2021/03/06/wintering-katherine-may/\">the self-renewal of wintering</a>. </p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_73395\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/05/cowarneredapple1811.jpg?resize=680%2C935&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"935\" class=\"size-full wp-image-73395\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/05/cowarneredapple1811.jpg?w=1000&#38;ssl=1 1000w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/05/cowarneredapple1811.jpg?resize=320%2C440&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/05/cowarneredapple1811.jpg?resize=600%2C825&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/05/cowarneredapple1811.jpg?resize=240%2C330&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/05/cowarneredapple1811.jpg?resize=768%2C1056&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">The Cowarne Apple, 1811. (Available <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/the-cowarne-red-apple-1811_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a print</a>, as a <a href=\"https://society6.com/brainpicker/collection/vintage-science-face-masks?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">face mask</a>, and as <a href=\"https://society6.com/brainpicker/collection/vintage-science-cards?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">stationery cards</a>, benefitting The Nature Conservancy.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>In <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Home-Place-Memoirs-Colored-Affair/dp/1571313508/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><strong><em>The Home Place: Memoirs of a Colored Man&#8217;s Love Affair with Nature</em></strong></a> (<a href=\"https://www.worldcat.org/title/home-place-memoirs-of-a-colored-mans-love-affair-with-nature/oclc/1012668431&#038;referer=brief_results\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><em>public library</em></a>) &#8212; his <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2021/04/21/j-drew-lanham-nature/\">love letter to the spirituality of science and the wonder of the wilderness</a> &#8212; the poetic ornithologist and wildlife ecologist <strong>J. Drew Lanham</strong> considers the singular and sensual enchantment of autumn:</p>\n<blockquote><p>Fall is the time when nature speaks most clearly to me. In autumn one is treated to an orgy of sights, sounds, and smells that can be wonderfully overwhelming. The stifling late-summer heat is mercifully cleared by cooler air overnight. Breathing is suddenly easier and the soaking sweat evaporates. You want to inhale deeply enough to take in every molecule wafting on the wind. The tired sameness of September’s deep green fades then flames into October’s vermilion sumacs and scarlet maples, lemon-yellow poplars and golden hickories. In those days of crispness I want to linger long enough to hear every sound and look far enough to see into forever.</p></blockquote>\n<p>Reflecting on the natural restlessness the season seems to stir in us and other animals, he writes:</p>\n<blockquote><p>The Germans have a fine word for it: <em>zugunruhe</em>. A compound derived from the roots <em>zug</em> (migration) and <em>unruhe</em> (anxiety), it describes the seasonal migration of birds and other animals. In this wanderlust I want to go somewhere far away, to fly to some place I think I need to be. Nature is on the move, too, migrating, storing, and dying. Everything is either accelerating or slowing down. Some things are rushing about to put in seed for the next generation. A monarch butterfly in a field full of goldenrod is urgent on tissue-thin wings of black and orange to gather the surging sweetness before the frost locks it away. Apple trees and tangles of muscadines hang heavy. The fruit-dense orchards offer a final call to the wildlings. Foxes, deer, coons, possum, and wild turkeys fatten in the feasting. The air is spiced with the scent of dying leaves. The perfume of decay gathers as berries ripen into wild wine. Even the sun sits differently in an autumnal sky, sending a mellower light in somber slants that foretell the coming change. </p>\n<p>The droning katydids, tired from their months-long work of filling the hot wet nights with song, hang on into October. But soon choirs of thousands dwindle to hundreds, and then just one or two. A persistent cricket tries hard to fiddle in time but the first freeze throws a wrench into his rhythm. The rustling riot of turning, falling leaves and the mysterious moonlit chirps of migrant songbirds winging their way to faraway places make my heart race&#8230; When the moon glows in a mid-November sky like a pallid sun, I, too, am so soaked in wanting and wood’s lust that I might as well wander like a warbler in the joyous urgency of it all.</p></blockquote>\n<figure id=\"attachment_71961\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/the-triumph-of-life_print?curator=brainpickier\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/TheTriumphOfLife_MariaPopova.jpg?resize=680%2C907&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"907\" class=\"size-full wp-image-71961\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/TheTriumphOfLife_MariaPopova.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/TheTriumphOfLife_MariaPopova.jpg?resize=240%2C320&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/TheTriumphOfLife_MariaPopova.jpg?resize=320%2C427&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/TheTriumphOfLife_MariaPopova.jpg?resize=768%2C1024&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/TheTriumphOfLife_MariaPopova.jpg?resize=600%2C800&#38;ssl=1 600w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\"><em>The Triumph of Life</em> by Maria Popova. (Available <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/the-triumph-of-life_print?curator=brainpickier\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a print</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Complement with Henry Beston &#8212; a father-figure for generations of such lyrical nature writers &#8212; on <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2016/09/16/henry-beston-northern-farm-harvest/\">harvest and the human spirit</a>, then revisit poet Diane Ackerman&#8217;s wonderful notion of <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2020/12/23/diane-ackerman-earth-ecstatic/\">living as an &#8220;Earth ecstatic&#8221;</a> and a <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2021/01/29/murmuration-linda-france/\">breathtaking animated poem</a> about our connection to nature and each other, inspired by the seasonal migration of starlings. </p>\n<hr /><h3>donating = loving</h3><p class=\"flipboard-keep\">For 15 years, I have been spending hundreds of hours and thousands of dollars each month to keep <em>Brain Pickings</em> going. It has remained free and ad-free and alive thanks to patronage from readers. I have no staff, no interns, no assistant — a thoroughly one-woman labor of love that is also my life and my livelihood. +0000","feedId":17,"bgimg":"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/lanham_thehomeplace.jpg?fit=320%2C495&ssl=1","linkMd5":"fc91fe384d1971e48faf58a95af79804","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn48@2020_2/2021/09/27/16-55-23-756_e0ffa1bbab460b8e.webp","destWidth":320,"destHeight":495,"sourceBytes":20110,"destBytes":20110,"author":"Maria Popova","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/lanham_thehomeplace.jpg?fit=320%2C495&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn48@2020_2/2021/09/27/16-55-23-756_e0ffa1bbab460b8e.webp","https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/05/cowarneredapple1811.jpg?resize=680%2C935&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn73@2020_3/2021/09/27/16-55-34-450_154102ebe7e1a3d7.webp","https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/TheTriumphOfLife_MariaPopova.jpg?resize=680%2C907&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx29/cdn16@2020_3/2021/09/27/16-55-33-373_5731796f0ecc8880.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/brainpickings/rss/~4/_UOEZaBvgKc":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn59@2020_5/2021/09/27/16-55-33-991_f7c7ab41fb66b694.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1632761707369},{"createdTime":"2021-09-28 00:55:06","updatedTime":"2021-09-28 00:55:06","title":"The Music of Trees: Improvisation, Iteration, and the Science of Immortality","link":"https://www.brainpickings.org/?p=74318","description":"<h3>&#8220;Potentially, every tree is immortal.&#8221;</h3>\n<hr>\n<p><a href=\"https://orionmagazine.org/product/oldgrowth/\" target=\"_blank\"><img width=\"320\" height=\"470\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/oldgrowth_orion.jpg?fit=320%2C470&#38;ssl=1\" class=\"cover alignright size-medium\" alt=\"The Music of Trees: Improvisation, Iteration, and the Science of Immortality\" loading=\"lazy\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/oldgrowth_orion.jpg?w=549&#38;ssl=1 549w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/oldgrowth_orion.jpg?resize=320%2C470&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/oldgrowth_orion.jpg?resize=240%2C352&#38;ssl=1 240w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 320px) 100vw, 320px\" /></a></p><p>Hermann Hesse <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2020/05/04/natascha-mcelhone-wander-hesse-kew/\">believed</a> that if we could learn to listen to the trees, we would achieve profound perspective on our human lives by grasping the deepest meaning of aliveness. He used listening in the metaphorical sense. But the great existential gift of trees &#8212; to us in the metaphors they furnish, and to themselves in the materiality of survival &#8212; might indeed be a kind of musicality, accounting for their <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2021/03/06/wintering-katherine-may/\">virtuosity at resilience</a>: beyond <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2018/05/14/jane-hirshfield-optimism-kelli-anderson-animation/\">&#8220;the blind optimism&#8221;</a> of a tree&#8217;s poetic enchantment lies a supersense for listening to the world and responding with inspired ingenuity, encoded with singular wisdom on how to live and how to die.</p>\n<p>So suggests arborist <strong>William Bryant Logan</strong> in his contribution to <a href=\"https://orionmagazine.org/product/oldgrowth/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><strong><em>Old Growth</em></strong></a> &#8212; a wondrous anthology of essays and poems about trees, culled from the decades-deep archive of <a href=\"https://orionmagazine.org\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><em>Orion Magazine</em></a>, with contributions as varied as Ursula K. Le Guin and Michael Pollan, and a foreword by the <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2015/05/13/gathering-moss-robin-wall-kimmerer/\">poetic bryologist</a> Robin Wall Kimmerer. </p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_70184\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/perspective5862218_print?sku=s6-21681426p4a1v1?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2020/03/Giant_by_MariaPopova.jpg?resize=680%2C907&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"907\" class=\"size-full wp-image-70184\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2020/03/Giant_by_MariaPopova.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2020/03/Giant_by_MariaPopova.jpg?resize=240%2C320&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2020/03/Giant_by_MariaPopova.jpg?resize=320%2C427&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2020/03/Giant_by_MariaPopova.jpg?resize=768%2C1024&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2020/03/Giant_by_MariaPopova.jpg?resize=600%2C800&#38;ssl=1 600w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\"><em>Perspective</em> by Maria Popova. (Available <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/perspective5862218_print?sku=s6-21681426p4a1v1?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a print</a>, benefitting The Nature Conservancy.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>In an essay titled &#8220;The Things Trees Know,&#8221; Bryant writes:</p>\n<blockquote><p>To study how trees grow is to admire not only their persistence but also their imagination. Live wood just won’t quit. Every time you knock it down, it comes back again, but when a plant sprouts back, it is not a random shot, like some finger simply raised to make a point. Rather, the growing tip of any stem &#8212; what botanists call the meristem &#8212; answers with an inborn, complex pattern, like a musical tune.</p></blockquote>\n<p>He draws out the musical analogy, reflecting on Charlie Parker&#8217;s famous advice to young musicians on the steps to becoming a true jazz artist: learn the instrument, learn the tunes, and only then soar with the skilled freedom of improvisation that makes jazz. Pointing to Coltrane&#8217;s &#8220;My Favorite Things&#8221; as a perfect embodiment of that three-step triumph, Bryant writes:</p>\n<blockquote><p>It begins with a perfectly clean statement of the tune, beautiful in itself for the richness of its tone, notes that are almost solid, so you could build a house out of them. Within three minutes, the tune has modulated into completely unexpected shapes, sizes, rising and falling glissades, stops and starts, pianissimos to fortes, but it never loses the thread of that original tune. Every tree is a jazz player, in just this way, although where a long Coltrane piece might last a quarter hour, a tree’s performance may go on for half a millennium or more.</p></blockquote>\n<p>Understanding a particular tree, Bryant argues, is a matter of discerning &#8220;its notes, its scales, its sharps, its flats, and its time signatures.&#8221; In the 1970s, the botanists Francis Hallé, Roelof Oldeman, and P. B. Tomlinson identified six sets of choices, which serve as the chords that every tree combines to compose its particular tune: to branch (most trees) or not to branch (palms); if branching, to branch only at the base of the stem or all along it; to grow new branches only upward (staghorn sumac), only outward (pagoda dogwood), or in some combination of the two; to grow each branch in a continuous upward or downward direction determined at its outset, or to change direction as it grows; to flower at the tips of branches (staghorn sumac) or along their sides (maple); to grow the trunk and branches continuously without rest or to have a dormant season. </p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_73031\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/winter-moon-at-toyamagahara-by-hasui-kawase-1931_print?sku=s6-19564919p4a1v46?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase3.jpg?resize=680%2C1005&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"1005\" class=\"size-full wp-image-73031\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase3.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase3.jpg?resize=320%2C473&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase3.jpg?resize=600%2C887&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase3.jpg?resize=240%2C355&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase3.jpg?resize=768%2C1135&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase3.jpg?resize=1039%2C1536&#38;ssl=1 1039w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\"><em>Winter Moon at Toyamagahara</em> by <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2021/03/22/hasui-kawase-prints/\">Hasui Kawase</a>, 1931. (Available <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/winter-moon-at-toyamagahara-by-hasui-kawase-1931_print?sku=s6-19564919p4a1v46?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a print</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Bryant writes:</p>\n<blockquote><p>Out of these six choices, each plant plays its tune, the phrase that has characterized its kind for millions of years. No matter where its seed sprouts, each will try to play its melody.</p></blockquote>\n<p>The tree does this by a process of deft improvisation attuned to the myriad chance-conditions and events of its environment, changing the scale of its melody as needed. (This reminds me of Coltrane&#8217;s own observation that jazz musicians are born with a certain feeling <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2021/07/06/john-coltrane-creative-urge/\">&#8220;that just comes out no matter what conditions exist.&#8221;</a>) Botanists call the tree&#8217;s responsive improvisation <em>reiteration</em>. Bryant writes:</p>\n<blockquote><p>It is jazz: take the tune, stretch it, cut it into pieces, put them back together, transpose it up or down, flatten it out, or shoot it at the sky. Each tree gets its chops, gets its charts, and then throws them away. It knows the chart by heart, and so can repeat it with a thousand variations for hundreds of years, as it grows to its full stature, lives among its peers, and grows back down to the ground. Positive and negative morphogenesis, they dubbed the cycle: growing up and growing down.</p>\n<p>As soon as the tune is played, the initial reiteration is the first major branch. As a leafy tree grows, it will generate what arborists call scaffold branches. These are the few &#8212; maybe five to eight &#8212; very large stems upon which the tree will hang most of its crown &#8212; that is, most of its smaller branches and their millions of leaves&#8230; The skill of the tree as an organism is like Coltrane in his vamping: it brings the variations back to the persisting theme.</p></blockquote>\n<p>In his <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2020/05/04/natascha-mcelhone-wander-hesse-kew/\">classic love letter to trees</a>, penned long before the science of reiteration was understood, Hesse observed that trees &#8220;struggle with all the force of their lives for one thing only: to fulfill themselves according to their own laws&#8221; &#8212; that is, to play their tune. But as much as they might be, in Hesse&#8217;s words, &#8220;the most penetrating preachers&#8221; in the art of living, they have at least as much to teach us about the art of dying. Beyond the already disorienting science of <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2020/10/21/turing-natural-wonders/\">why a tree, like a human being, is partly dead throughout life</a>, trees are living testaments to Richard Dawkins&#8217;s wonderful perspective on <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2021/07/25/richard-dawkins-death/\">the luckiness of dying</a>, virtuosos at the art of letting life go with the same purposeful poise with which it is lived. </p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_74023\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/possible-certainties_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/PossibleCertainties_by_MariaPopova.jpg?resize=680%2C850&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"850\" class=\"size-full wp-image-74023\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/PossibleCertainties_by_MariaPopova.jpg?w=1000&#38;ssl=1 1000w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/PossibleCertainties_by_MariaPopova.jpg?resize=320%2C400&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/PossibleCertainties_by_MariaPopova.jpg?resize=600%2C750&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/PossibleCertainties_by_MariaPopova.jpg?resize=240%2C300&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/PossibleCertainties_by_MariaPopova.jpg?resize=768%2C960&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\"><em>Possible Certainties</em> by Maria Popova. (Available <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/possible-certainties_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a print</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Citing a common saying about oaks &#8212; “Three hundred years growing, three hundred years living, three hundred years dying.” &#8212; Bryant considers the third stage of a tree&#8217;s life, known as negative morphogenesis, or “growing down”:</p>\n<blockquote><p>Growing down is not just decay. It is as active and improvisational as was the building up. Roots are damaged or die. Branches are lost to storms. Hollows open up on the trunk and are colonized by fungi like the wonderful and aptly named dryad’s saddle. The tree’s solid circulation system resolves itself back into discrete pathways, some living and some dead. It becomes obvious that scaffold branches were once separate trees, as they become so again, some maintaining their root systems and others losing them. Now the tips of the higher branches begin to die back. Instead of growing new reiteration branchlets on their undersides, as they did in their youth, they now sprout perfect little trees of their species on the tops of the branches, between the trunk and the dead tips. It is a complete restatement of the thematic tune, happening dozens of times among the still-living branches.</p></blockquote>\n<p>What unfolds in this dying stage is a process known as <em>Phoenix regeneration</em>:</p>\n<blockquote><p>Little by little, a tree loses its crown, first small branches, then larger ones. Roots decay. The circulation system that carries water aloft to the leaves starts to break down. When no leaves emerge on a branch, it can no longer feed itself. It dies and falls to the ground, but the tree does not give up. When a giant that was once ninety feet tall has shrunk to a height of twenty feet, little images of itself may sprout from the lower trunk or even from the root flare, wherever a living connection between root and branch survives&#8230; It is not impossible that one or the other of those last sprouts &#8212; if only they can generate their own stable root systems &#8212; may grow once again to ninety feet tall&#8230; Potentially, every tree is immortal.</p></blockquote>\n<figure id=\"attachment_71908\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2020/11/06/trees-rustle-tara-books/\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/The-Leaf-Tree.jpg?resize=600%2C700&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"600\" height=\"700\" class=\"size-full wp-image-71908\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/The-Leaf-Tree.jpg?w=600&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/The-Leaf-Tree.jpg?resize=240%2C280&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/The-Leaf-Tree.jpg?resize=320%2C373&#38;ssl=1 320w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">The <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2020/11/06/trees-rustle-tara-books/\">Leaf Tree</a> of indigenous Gond mythology, from  <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2011/09/20/the-night-life-of-trees-tara-books/\"><em>The Night Life of Trees</em></a>.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Recounting his encounter with a colossal long-fallen Osage orange tree, from the dead trunk of which two miraculous former branches had risen vertically as new trunks lush with life, Bryant returns to his musical improvisation analogy: </p>\n<blockquote><p>It is as though a person rested her arm on the dirt, spread out her palm, and two perfect new arms emerged from her lifeline, complete with all the muscles and tendons and circulation, the hands, palms, fingers, and fingernails. Or perhaps more accurate, as though a person lay down at night and had two new people overnight sprout from his torso, complete from toenails to cowlicks. I think John Coltrane would have loved phoenix regeneration. It is like those moments in “My Favorite Things” where the whole piece seems about to jump off the top end of the soprano sax register, but suddenly the tune takes up again.</p></blockquote>\n<p><a href=\"https://orionmagazine.org/product/oldgrowth/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><strong><em>Old Growth</em></strong></a> is a trove of wonder and wisdom in its entirety. Complement this fragment with Dylan Thomas&#8217;s short, splendid poem about <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2020/10/27/dylan-thomas-being-but-men/\">trees and the wonder of being human</a>, Thoreau on <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2020/01/20/thoreau-trees/\">the true value of a tree</a>, and forester and biomimicry pioneer Janine Benyus on <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2021/07/22/all-we-can-save-janine-benyus/\">how the astonishing science of &#8220;tree islands&#8221; illuminates the key to resilience</a>.</p>\n<hr /><h3>donating = loving</h3><p class=\"flipboard-keep\">For 15 years, I have been spending hundreds of hours and thousands of dollars each month to keep <em>Brain Pickings</em> going.
