Popova","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/whatisariver.jpg?fit=320%2C319&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn31@2020_3/2021/09/27/16-55-27-941_57bdd0e5b9a2c439.webp","https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/whatisariver20.jpg?resize=680%2C447&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx3/cdn97@2020_5/2021/09/27/16-55-37-251_f7f5a83243e38d16.webp","https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/whatisariver1.jpg?resize=680%2C346&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn25@2020_5/2021/09/27/16-55-35-722_f414c6f3ef9d0af1.webp","https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/whatisariver21.jpg?resize=680%2C468&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx19/cdn7@2020_1/2021/09/27/16-55-34-346_82392492c5f03b1c.webp","https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/whatisariver5.jpg?resize=680%2C346&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn43@2020_5/2021/09/27/16-55-33-656_278562ffd0b6df7d.webp","https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/whatisariver3.jpg?resize=680%2C346&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn68@2020_4/2021/09/27/16-55-34-099_72f4b2d7b9f9f99e.webp","https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/whatisariver2.jpg?resize=680%2C346&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn6@2020_6/2021/09/27/16-55-33-210_d71cbffdc72c01c1.webp","https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/whatisariver22.jpg?resize=680%2C447&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn32@2020_3/2021/09/27/16-55-34-131_2b4a2dd36c0ca993.webp","https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/whatisariver23.jpg?resize=680%2C453&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn65@2020_4/2021/09/27/16-55-35-398_7d9aca5305159b6c.webp","https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/whatisariver4.jpg?resize=680%2C346&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn72@2020_5/2021/09/27/16-55-33-734_2c730583ecdb4a1b.webp","https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/whatisariver10.jpg?resize=680%2C692&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn52@2020_2/2021/09/27/16-55-33-705_eb154f4920d3a0df.webp","https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/whatisariver6.jpg?resize=680%2C346&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn78@2020_6/2021/09/27/16-55-34-674_661f6c79fbd27263.webp","https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/whatisariver25.jpg?resize=680%2C427&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx24/cdn87@2020_3/2021/09/27/16-55-34-213_d60bb3cc357f8229.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/brainpickings/rss/~4/-C2Tglv0sQo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn71@2020_4/2021/09/27/16-55-33-124_a98b5e1b1491c447.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1632761706659},{"createdTime":"2021-09-28 00:55:07","updatedTime":"2021-09-28 00:55:07","title":"Music and the Mystery of Aliveness","link":"https://www.brainpickings.org/?p=74167","description":"<h3>&#8220;We are a music-making species — always have been, always will be — and music’s capacity to explore, express and address what it is to be human remains one of our greatest communal gifts.&#8221;</h3>\n<hr>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Year-Wonder-Classical-Music-Enjoy/dp/0062856200/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\"><img width=\"320\" height=\"480\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/yearofwonder_clemency.jpg?fit=320%2C480&#38;ssl=1\" class=\"cover alignright size-medium\" alt=\"Music and the Mystery of Aliveness\" loading=\"lazy\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/yearofwonder_clemency.jpg?w=1600&#38;ssl=1 1600w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/yearofwonder_clemency.jpg?resize=320%2C480&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/yearofwonder_clemency.jpg?resize=600%2C900&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/yearofwonder_clemency.jpg?resize=240%2C360&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/yearofwonder_clemency.jpg?resize=768%2C1152&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/yearofwonder_clemency.jpg?resize=1024%2C1536&#38;ssl=1 1024w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/yearofwonder_clemency.jpg?resize=1365%2C2048&#38;ssl=1 1365w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 320px) 100vw, 320px\" /></a></p><p>“Sound is sea: pattern lapping pattern&#8230; Matter delights in music, and became Bach,” the poet Ronald Johnson wrote as he contemplated <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2021/05/30/ronald-johnson-ark-music/\">matter, music, and the mind</a>.</p>\n<p>A generation after him, a young woman discovered that when the mind is suddenly unmattered, Bach remains.</p>\n<p>One midwinter day shortly before the pandemic paralyzed the world, Clemency Burton-Hill &#8212; an underground London garage DJ turned BBC host turned creative director of America&#8217;s oldest public radio station for classical music, and a lifelong lover of Bach &#8212; suffered a catastrophic hemorrhage in her left frontal lobe. She was thirty-nine, her children one and five. She survived, but was left unable to see, move, or speak. </p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_74176\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/clemencyburtonhill_wnyc.jpg?resize=680%2C680&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"680\" class=\"size-full wp-image-74176\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/clemencyburtonhill_wnyc.jpg?w=1860&#38;ssl=1 1860w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/clemencyburtonhill_wnyc.jpg?resize=320%2C320&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/clemencyburtonhill_wnyc.jpg?resize=600%2C600&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/clemencyburtonhill_wnyc.jpg?resize=240%2C240&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/clemencyburtonhill_wnyc.jpg?resize=768%2C768&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/clemencyburtonhill_wnyc.jpg?resize=1536%2C1536&#38;ssl=1 1536w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/clemencyburtonhill_wnyc.jpg?w=1360&#38;ssl=1 1360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Clemency Burton Hill (Portrait: Matthew Septimus / WNYC)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Multiple surgeries and weeks of rehabilitation began restoring Clemency&#8217;s comprehension and sight, but the right side of her body remained paralyzed and her speech voided. Slowly, slowly, the words started forming again out of the primeval matter of the mind. Eventually, we spoke &#8212; Clemency still in her hospital bed, skull bandaged and face radiant with life, each word a triumph, as deliberate and precise as a Bach note. I found myself wondering what the world might look like if we spoke to each other that way, our words tender with our mortal fragility, resolute with reverence for the aliveness in us and in each other, this grand shared mystery.</p>\n<p>Not long before her hemorrhage, Clemency had made a passionate case for a daily dose of music as &#8220;a form of sonic soul maintenance&#8221; in her book <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Year-Wonder-Classical-Music-Enjoy/dp/0062856200/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><strong><em>Year of Wonder: Classical Music to Enjoy Day by Day</em></strong></a> (<a href=\"https://www.worldcat.org/title/year-of-wonder-classical-music-to-enjoy-day-by-day/oclc/1078350287&#038;referer=brief_results\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><em>public library</em></a>) &#8212; the music counterpart to Tolstoy&#8217;s <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2013/03/15/a-calendar-of-wisdom-tolstoy/\"><em>Calendar of Wisdom</em></a> and poet Ross Gay&#8217;s <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2019/12/01/ross-gay-book-of-delights/\">yearlong journal of delights</a>. She wrote:</p>\n<blockquote><p>We are a music-making species &#8212; always have been, always will be &#8212; and music’s capacity to explore, express and address what it is to be human remains one of our greatest communal gifts&#8230; We evolved by coming together around the fire every night, singing songs and telling stories &#8212; invariably, telling stories through singing songs. That’s what our ancestors did; that’s how they made sense of the world and each other; that’s how they learned how to be.</p>\n<p>It is an impulse that is still fundamental to who we are.</p></blockquote>\n<p>Fittingly, the musical calendar of wonder begins with a Bach liturgy for January 1. Bach punctuates Clemency&#8217;s sonic year as a maker of music that &#8220;contains all of everything&#8221; and maker of &#8220;the blueprint for everything that was to come,&#8221; his influence reverberating through the hallway of time to shape genres as diverse as techno and funk. As the year unfolds, there are his <em>Goldberg Variations</em> with their exquisite mathematical precision, rumored to have been composed as an insomnia cure, their original manuscript bearing an inscription in Bach&#8217;s hand: <em>&#8220;Prepared for the soul’s delight of lovers of music.&#8221;</em> </p>\n<p>There is his violin solo in E major that always comes as &#8220;a shot of musical caffeine&#8221; for Clemency: &#8220;In just a hundred seconds or so,&#8221; she writes, &#8220;this piece has the effect of apparently rearranging the molecules around me, making me see and think more clearly.&#8221; </p>\n<p>There is his <em>Ave Maria</em> in early June, and his Partita no. 2 in D Minor on my late-summer birthday, and on my father&#8217;s autumnal equinox birthday a chorale cantata translating to <em>&#8220;As a father has mercy.&#8221;</em> (This, too, is Bach&#8217;s singular enchantment &#8212; how we project ourselves onto him and focus our own existence through his lens.) </p>\n<p>Bach&#8217;s diurnal presence took on a new form after Clemency&#8217;s hemorrhage and became an embodied testament to philosopher Josef Pieper&#8217;s soulful case for <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2017/07/27/josef-pieper-only-the-lover-sings/\">how Bach can save your soul</a>. At first, with her life so brutally transformed, she found it difficult to even listen to his music, hearing in it the echoes of her former life and former self. But she eventually came to see Bach for what he always had been and always would be &#8212; the existential soundtrack to aliveness itself. </p>\n<p>Along the protracted trajectory of her recovery, both physical and psychological, Clemency began not only listening to but playing Bach every single day. &#8220;To recover the Bach in me,&#8221; she says in her <a href=\"https://www.bbc.co.uk/programmes/m000ytzj\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">stunning BBC piece</a> about the experience &#8212; her first word-work since that savage January day, and the most moving audio artwork I have heard in epochs. </p>\n<p>With her hard-won words, she invites the voices of people from various walks of life, people who all play Bach daily to move through their own very different and differently challenging lives &#8212; from an elderly organist in Germany to a young cellist and community organizer in Kenya&#8217;s largest slum: Bach as meditation, Bach as motivation, Bach as calibration of being. (When we spoke that day from the hospital, I shared with Clemency something hardly anyone in my life knew: that I was a secret cellist, still learning the instrument, playing a single Bach cello suite day after day as I waded through a very different personal loss.)</p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_74177\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/cello_by_MariaPopova.jpg?resize=680%2C547&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"547\" class=\"size-full wp-image-74177\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/cello_by_MariaPopova.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/cello_by_MariaPopova.jpg?resize=320%2C258&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/cello_by_MariaPopova.jpg?resize=600%2C483&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/cello_by_MariaPopova.jpg?resize=240%2C193&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/cello_by_MariaPopova.jpg?resize=768%2C618&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Nina, my cello.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>In exploring Bach as a daily ritual, Clemency draws on the legacy of the legendary Spanish Catalan cellist and conductor <strong>Pablo Casals</strong> (December 29, 1876&#8211;October 22, 1973) &#8212; Yo-Yo Ma&#8217;s hero and formative influence, widely considered the greatest cellist of all time, who at the age of ninety-three reflected so tenderly on <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2014/12/03/pablo-casals-work-age/\">how working with love prolongs your life</a>. Casals began <a href=\"http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0671217747/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">his autobiography</a> by sharing the daily practice that had anchored him to his own life since the day he first fell under Bach&#8217;s enchantment: </p>\n<blockquote><p>For the past eighty years I have started each day in the same manner. It is not a mechanical routine but something essential to my daily life. I go to the piano, and I play two preludes and fugues of Bach. I cannot think of doing otherwise. It is a sort of benediction on the house&#8230; It is a rediscovery of the world of which I have the joy of being a part. It fills me with awareness of the wonder of life, with a feeling of the incredible marvel of being a human being. The music is never the same for me, never. Each day it is something new, fantastic and unbelievable.</p></blockquote>\n<figure  class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/pablocasals4.jpg?resize=600%2C306&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"600\" height=\"306\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-74175\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/pablocasals4.jpg?w=600&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/pablocasals4.jpg?resize=320%2C163&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/pablocasals4.jpg?resize=240%2C122&#38;ssl=1 240w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Pablo Casals</figcaption></figure>\n<p>In Bach, Casals found an analogue for the miracle of nature. Echoing the poet and philosopher of science Loren Eiseley&#8217;s poignant observation that <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2017/06/22/loren-eiseley-muskrat/\">&#8220;we forget that nature itself is one vast miracle transcending the reality of night and nothingness&#8230; that each one of us in his personal life repeats that miracle,&#8221;</a> Casals reflected on his profound personal connection to nature, of which his love of music was an expression &#8212; a way to feel more alive, more awake to the wonder of aliveness:</p>\n<blockquote><p>I do not think a day passes in my life in which I fail to look with fresh amazement at the miracle of nature. It is there on every side. It can be simply a shadow on a mountainside, or a spider&#8217;s web gleaming with dew, or sunlight on the leaves of a tree. I have always especially loved the sea. Whenever possible, I have lived by the sea.</p></blockquote>\n<p>The sea and Bach were always intimately connected for Casals, who fell under Bach&#8217;s spell at thirteen. One saltwater-scented afternoon, his father bought him his first full-sized cello &#8212; an instrument looked down upon in Bach&#8217;s day, too unworthy to compose solos for. Father and son then walked to a musty old music shop in the nearby harbor &#8212; Casals never forgot &#8220;its faint smell of the sea&#8221; &#8212; where he acquired his other great portal into the &#8220;magic and mystery&#8221; of music: a yellowed sheaf of scores, faded with age, bearing the title <em>Six Suites for Violoncello Solo</em>, imprinted with &#8220;J.S. Bach.&#8221; They became his most cherished music. </p>\n<p>A lifetime later, looking back on how these cello suites had grown to be regarded as &#8220;academic works, mechanical, without warmth&#8221; in the century and a half since Bach&#8217;s death in 1750, and how no cellist or violinist had performed any of them in its entirety, Casals exclaimed:</p>\n<blockquote><p>How could anyone think of them as being cold, when a whole radiance of space and poetry pours forth from them! They are the very essence of Bach, and Bach is the essence of music.</p></blockquote>\n<p>Casals and his generation had awakened to the radiance of Bach thanks to his contemporary and hero <strong>Albert Schweitzer</strong> (January 14, 1875&#8211;September 4, 1965). Although Schweitzer received the Nobel Peace Prize for his ethical-ecological philosophy of &#8220;Reverence for Life&#8221; &#8212; the philosophy that inspired sea-serenader Rachel Carson to dedicate her epoch-making <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2017/01/27/rachel-carson-silent-spring-dorothy-freeman/\"><em>Silent Spring</em></a> to Schweitzer &#8212; music always remained his greatest animating passion. </p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_74178\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/albertschweitzer.jpg?resize=680%2C659&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"659\" class=\"size-full wp-image-74178\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/albertschweitzer.jpg?w=1158&#38;ssl=1 1158w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/albertschweitzer.jpg?resize=320%2C310&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/albertschweitzer.jpg?resize=600%2C582&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/albertschweitzer.jpg?resize=240%2C233&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/albertschweitzer.jpg?resize=768%2C745&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Albert Schweitzer, early 1900s.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Schweitzer &#8212; born almost exactly 200 years after Bach, to a minister and a pastor&#8217;s daughter &#8212; was five when his father began giving him music lessons on the piano inherited from his organist grandfather. Before his legs were long enough to reach the pedals, the boy began playing the organ himself. By nine, he was substituting for the church organist at service. </p>\n<p>And then he discovered Bach.</p>\n<p>During the Classical and early Romantic eras that followed Bach&#8217;s, his music fell out of favor and slipped into academic obscurity, relegated to a thing of theory, syphoned of transcendence. The young Schweitzer, serving as an organist to the Paris Bach Society that he had co-founded while completing his doctoral dissertation on the spirituality of Kant&#8217;s philosophy at the Sorbonne, grew increasingly restless at this erasure of wonder and took it upon himself to remedy it. In those first years of the twentieth century, the only Bach material available to French readers &#8212; even those who cherished and played music &#8212; were only dry biographies that presented him as a cold mathematician of sound. A musician himself, Schweitzer longed to talk to other musicians and lovers of music about &#8220;the real nature of Bach’s music and its interpretation&#8221; &#8212; to resurrect Bach the artist, the enchanter, the virtuoso of feeling, the <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2020/01/27/michael-pollan-bach/\">prophet of transcendence</a>.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/J-S-Bach-Vol-1/dp/0486216314/?tag=brapick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img class=\"cover\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/schweitzer_bach.jpg?w=680&#038;ssl=1\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a>In 1902, Schweitzer spent his autumn vacation writing an essay to get the students at the Paris Conservatory excited about Bach. He quickly found himself with much more to say &#8212; so much more that, after using his meager funds to purchase a copy of Bach&#8217;s hard to find and extravagantly priced complete works, he spent the next two years turning the essay into a 455-page <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/J-S-Bach-Vol-1/dp/0486216314/?tag=brapick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">book</a> that introduced the world to Bach the artist; the book that magnetized a largehearted embrace when Casals met Schweitzer in the 1930s.</p>\n<p>In it, Schweitzer rescued Bach from the theorists who had coopted him for their ideologies of &#8220;pure music&#8221; &#8212; composition devoid of poetry, created solely as a mathematical exercise in harmonic perfection &#8212; and instead helped people see him as &#8220;a poet and painter in sound&#8221; who uses the language of music to paint entire landscapes of thought and feeling. He wrote:</p>\n<blockquote><p>The impulse to express poetic and pictorial concepts is the essence of music. It addresses itself to the listener’s creative imagination and seeks to kindle in him the feelings and visions with which the music was composed. But this it can do only if the person who uses the language of sound possesses the mysterious faculty of rendering thoughts with a superior clarity and precision. In this respect Bach is the greatest of the great&#8230; A soul that longs for peace out of the world’s unrest and has itself already tasted peace allows others to share its experience in this music.</p></blockquote>\n<p>Schweitzer observed that there are two types of artists: the subjective, who use their personality as the wellspring of their art and live as &#8220;a law unto themselves,&#8221; and the objective, whose &#8220;artistic personality exists independently of the human&#8221; and whose art is &#8220;not impersonal, but superpersonal,&#8221; channeling the universal and the eternal through the vessel of their being. Bach was such an artist:</p>\n<blockquote><p>It is as if he felt only one impulse, to express again what he already finds in existence, but to express it definitively, in unique perfection. It is not he who lives, it is the spirit of the time that lives in him. All the artistic endeavours, desires, creations, aspirations and errors of his own and of previous generations are concentrated and worked out to their conclusion in him.</p>\n<p>[&#8230;]</p>\n<p>Bach is thus a terminal point. Nothing comes from him; everything merely leads up to him&#8230;. This genius was not an individual, but a collective soul. Centuries and generations have laboured at this work, before the grandeur of which we halt in veneration. To anyone who has gone through the history of this epoch and knows what the end of it was, it is the history of that culminating spirit, as it was before it objectivated itself in a single personality. </p></blockquote>\n<p>He adds a poetic corollary to this eternal and aggregate nature of art:</p>\n<blockquote><p>We feel it to be a matter of course that some day a Bach shall come in whom all those, other Bachs shall find a posthumous existence.</p></blockquote>\n<p>The book project interrupted the young Schweitzer&#8217;s theological writings and accompanied him on the path to medical school, with Bach as his bridge between spirituality and science. Struggling financially, he paid for his medical education with proceeds from the Bach book and income from his Bach concerts. </p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_74169\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/benshahn_bach.jpg?resize=680%2C665&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"665\" class=\"size-full wp-image-74169\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/benshahn_bach.jpg?w=885&#38;ssl=1 885w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/benshahn_bach.jpg?resize=320%2C313&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/benshahn_bach.jpg?resize=600%2C586&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/benshahn_bach.jpg?resize=240%2C235&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/benshahn_bach.jpg?resize=768%2C751&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Albert Schweitzer at his organ. LP cover art by <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2016/11/08/ben-shahn-the-shape-of-content-norton-nonconformity/\">Ben Shahn</a>.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>His passionate appreciation of Bach never left him. A decade later, as he headed for Africa to do the work out of which his philosophy of &#8220;Reverence for Life&#8221; arose &#8212; the work that earned him the Nobel Peace Prize and Rachel Carson&#8217;s devotion &#8212; Schweitzer brought with him a pedal piano the Paris Bach Society had given him as the closest thing to an organ one could bring to the tropics so he could continue his daily Bach. In his autobiography, he reflected:</p>\n<blockquote><p>During the many peaceful hours I was able to spend with Bach during my four and a half years in the jungle I had penetrated deeper into the spirit of his works.</p></blockquote>\n<p>Hatcheting her way through the synaptic jungle, Clemency too found herself in more intimate contact with the spirit of Bach&#8217;s music, unfolding <a href=\"https://www.bbc.co.uk/programmes/m000ytzj\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">&#8220;the ultimate expression of anything and everything&#8221;</a> &#8212; aliveness and mortality cleaved into the edge of being, the edge on which we are all perched every instant of every living day, each moment more precarious than we dare think, each more precious than we dare feel. How poignant to reread now this passage from <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Year-Wonder-Classical-Music-Enjoy/dp/0062856200/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><strong><em>Year of Wonder</em></strong></a> &#8212; a book Clemency wrote out of her belief, then only mental but not yet matter-tested, that &#8220;music holds the mystery of being alive&#8221;; that something singular happens &#8220;when we open up our lives to let such music in&#8221;:</p>\n<blockquote><p>Bach’s brain was clearly some kind of supercomputer: he wrote at least three thousand pieces whilst holding down a number of jobs, a couple of wives and twenty children.</p>\n<p>[&#8230;]</p>\n<p>The essence of what makes Bach the greatest eludes words, but it lies, I think, in the way he combines technical precision with socking great emotion. People often describe Bach as ‘mathematical’ because of the complex, intricate patterns in his music. But he is not clinical or scientific: as a human being he knew intense joy but also wild grief, and there’s never been a composer or songwriter more attuned to the vagaries of the human heart.</p></blockquote>\n<hr /><h3>donating = loving</h3><p class=\"flipboard-keep\">For 15 years, I have been spending hundreds of hours and thousands of dollars each month to keep <em>Brain Pickings</em> going. 00:55:07","updatedTime":"2021-09-28 00:55:07","title":"Recovering the Wonder of Flight: “Little Prince” Author Antoine de Saint-Exupéry on Finding the Miraculous in the Mechanical","link":"https://www.brainpickings.org/?p=74156","description":"<h3>&#8220;In anything at all, perfection is finally attained not when there is no longer anything to add, but when there is no longer anything to take away, when a body has been stripped down to its nakedness.&#8221;</h3>\n<hr>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Wind-Sand-Stars-Antoine-Saint-Exupery/dp/1388227479/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\"><img width=\"300\" height=\"456\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/05/windsandandstars_exupery.jpg?fit=300%2C456&#38;ssl=1\" class=\"cover alignright size-medium\" alt=\"Recovering the Wonder of Flight: &#8220;Little Prince&#8221; Author Antoine de Saint-Exupéry on Finding the Miraculous in the Mechanical\" loading=\"lazy\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/05/windsandandstars_exupery.jpg?w=300&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/05/windsandandstars_exupery.jpg?resize=240%2C365&#38;ssl=1 240w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 300px) 100vw, 300px\" /></a></p><p>I am sitting on an airplane, uneasy and grateful amid the sea of masks. </p>\n<p>I am sitting on an airplane &#8212; this silver triumph of physics and imagination centuries in the dreaming &#8212; watching the cotton-candy cloudscape below with wonder bordering on ecstasy that will never, for me, grow old. </p>\n<p>I am thinking about my grandmother, who was already a grandmother by the time she flew for the first time, having seen an airplane only once before, in the forest by the remote Bulgarian mountain village of her wartime childhood &#8212; a fighter plane shot down to fall from sky into the life and imagination of a little girl wide-eyed with wonder and terror. </p>\n<p>I am thinking, too, of <em>Little Prince</em> author <strong>Antoine de Saint-Exupéry</strong> (June 29, 1900&#8211;July 31, 1944), whose experience as a pilot during that same war sculpted <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2019/05/14/antoine-de-saint-exupery-night/\">his understanding of mortality and meaning</a>, inspiring his timeless masterwork of philosophy disguised as a children&#8217;s book &#8212; my favorite of all time.</p>\n<p>In a passage from <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Wind-Sand-Stars-Antoine-Saint-Exupery/dp/1388227479/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><strong><em>Wind, Sand, and Stars</em></strong></a> (<a href=\"https://www.worldcat.org/title/wind-sand-and-stars/oclc/1045205465&#038;referer=brief_results\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><em>public library</em></a>) &#8212; that slender, poetic collection of his life-drawn meditations on life &#8212; he reverences the elegant and daring miracle of flight, a miracle we have come to take for granted in a mere two generations as the technology behind it has exponentially improved to make it even more miraculous. (I am writing this on a book-sized machine that can access through the air nearly all the knowledge humanity has produced, and I am doing that while suspended in the middle of the sky &#8212; what would Kepler have made of this, or his mother, who <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2019/12/26/katharina-kepler-witchcraft-dream/\">paid for the kernel of this miracle with her life</a>?)</p>\n<figure  class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/dp/0809479702/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2014/04/exupery3.jpg?w=680&#038;ssl=1\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Antoine de Saint-Exupéry</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Saint-Exupéry writes:</p>\n<blockquote><p>In anything at all, perfection is finally attained not when there is no longer anything to add, but when there is no longer anything to take away, when a body has been stripped down to its nakedness.</p>\n<p>[&#8230;]</p>\n<p>There is an ancient myth about the image asleep in the block of marble until it is carefully disengaged by the sculptor. The sculptor must himself feel that he is not so much inventing or shaping the curve of breast or shoulder as delivering the image from its prison. </p>\n<p>In this spirit do engineers, physicists concerned with thermodynamics, and the swarm of preoccupied draughtsmen tackle their work. In appearance, but only in appearance, they seem to be polishing surfaces and refining away angles, easing this joint or stabilizing that wing, rendering these parts invisible, so that in the end there is no longer a wing hooked to a framework but a form flawless in its perfection, completely disengaged from its matrix, a sort of spontaneous whole, its parts mysteriously fused together and resembling in their unity a poem.</p></blockquote>\n<p>It was a countercultural notion then, and it is even more so today, this idea that the mechanical can become not the enemy of but a portal to the poetic, the miraculous &#8212; a lovely reminder that in how we orient ourselves to anything lies the whole of its valence. </p>\n<figure  class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2014/05/27/the-pilot-and-the-little-prince-peter-sis/\"><img src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2014/05/pilotlittleprince_sis12.jpg\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Art by Peter Sís from <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2014/05/27/the-pilot-and-the-little-prince-peter-sis/\"><em>The Pilot and the Little Prince</em></a> &#8212; his tender illustrated biography of and tribute to Antoine de Saint-Exupéry and his masterpiece.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Saint-Exupéry extends the invitation to reorient to this particular skyborne machine &#8212; and, by a proximate leap of imagination, to technology in general &#8212; as something that, rather than alienating us from the rest of nature, could bring us into more intimate and conscientious contact with the world of clouds and creatures:</p>\n<blockquote><p>Startling as it is that all visible evidence of invention should have been refined out of this instrument and that there should be delivered to us an object as natural as a pebble polished by the waves, it is equally wonderful that he who uses this instrument should be able to forget that it is a machine&#8230; We forget that motors are whirring: the motor, finally, has come to fulfill its function, which is to whirr as a heart beats &#8212; and we give no thought to the beating of our heart. Thus, precisely because it is perfect the machine dissembles its own existence instead of forcing itself upon our notice. </p>\n<p>And thus, also, the realities of nature resume their pride of place&#8230; The machine does not isolate man from the great problems of nature but plunges him more deeply into them.</p></blockquote>\n<figure  class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2014/02/03/exupery-little-prince-morgan-drawings/\"><img src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2014/01/thelittleprince_morgan9.jpg\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">One of Saint-Exupéry&#8217;s <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2014/02/03/exupery-little-prince-morgan-drawings/\">original watercolors for <em>The Little Prince</em></a>.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Complement with the uncommonly poetic scientist and philosopher Loren Eiseley on <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2017/06/22/loren-eiseley-muskrat/\">reclaiming our sense of the miraculous in a mechanical age</a>, then revisit Saint-Exupéry on <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2019/05/28/antoine-de-saint-exupery-wind-sand-and-stars/\">losing a friend</a> and <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2014/04/18/antoine-de-saint-exupery-letter-to-a-hostage-smile/\">how a simple smile saved his life during the war</a>.</p>\n<hr /><h3>donating = loving</h3><p class=\"flipboard-keep\">For 15 years, I have been spending hundreds of hours and thousands of dollars each month to keep <em>Brain Pickings</em> going. It has remained free and ad-free and alive thanks to patronage from readers. I have no staff, no interns, no assistant — a thoroughly one-woman labor of love that is also my life and my livelihood. Popova","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/05/windsandandstars_exupery.jpg?fit=300%2C456&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx29/cdn94@2020_3/2021/09/27/16-55-12-062_c4428627ce60d7e7.webp","https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2014/04/exupery3.jpg?w=680&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx5oss/cdn28@2020_2/2021/09/27/16-55-33-400_3b3dec7850e1c035.webp","https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2014/05/pilotlittleprince_sis12.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn72@2020_2/2021/09/27/16-55-34-230_bb0b66b0280b18c5.webp","https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2014/01/thelittleprince_morgan9.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn11@2020_3/2021/09/27/16-55-33-965_95d199cca9d6a71f.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/brainpickings/rss/~4/NK8Jms6Y0oo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx29/cdn28@2020_6/2021/09/27/16-55-33-882_bd80d0154498fdcf.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1632761707374},{"createdTime":"2021-09-28 00:55:06","updatedTime":"2021-09-28 00:55:06","title":"The Good Luck of Your Bad Luck: Marcus Aurelius on the Stoic Strategy for Weathering Life’s Waves and Turning Suffering into Strength","link":"https://www.brainpickings.org/?p=74432","description":"<h3>&#8220;What happened could have happened to anyone, but not everyone could have carried on.&#8221;</h3>\n<hr>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Meditations-Annotated-Marcus-Aurelius/dp/1541673859/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\"><img width=\"320\" height=\"496\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/meditations_robinwaterfield.jpg?fit=320%2C496&#38;ssl=1\" class=\"cover with-border alignright size-medium\" alt=\"The Good Luck of Your Bad Luck: Marcus Aurelius on the Stoic Strategy for Weathering Life&#8217;s Waves and Turning Suffering into Strength\" loading=\"lazy\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/meditations_robinwaterfield.jpg?w=645&#38;ssl=1 645w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/meditations_robinwaterfield.jpg?resize=320%2C496&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/meditations_robinwaterfield.jpg?resize=600%2C930&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/meditations_robinwaterfield.jpg?resize=240%2C372&#38;ssl=1 240w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 320px) 100vw, 320px\" /></a></p><p>Most people live with a great deal more suffering than is visible to even the most proximate and sensitive onlooker. Many have survived things both unimaginable and invisible to the outside world. This has been the case since the dawn of our species, for human nature has hardly changed beneath the continually repainted façade of our social sanctions &#8212; human beings have always been capable of inflicting tremendous pain on each other and capable of triumphal healing. </p>\n<p>There is, however, a peculiar modern phenomenon that might best be described as a culture of competitive trauma. In recent times, the touching human longing for sympathy, that impulse to have our suffering recognized and validated, has grown distorted by a troubling compulsion for broadcast-suffering and comparative validity. Personhoods are staked on the cards dealt and not the hands played, as if we evolved the opposable thumbs of our agency for nothing. In memoirs and reality shows, across infinite Alexandrian scrolls of social media feeds, the unlucky events of life have become the currency of attention and identification. </p>\n<figure  class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/last-appeal-from-trees-at-night-by-art-young_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/08/artyoung_treesatnight7.jpg?resize=680%2C1070&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"1070\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-68434\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/08/artyoung_treesatnight7.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/08/artyoung_treesatnight7.jpg?resize=240%2C378&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/08/artyoung_treesatnight7.jpg?resize=320%2C503&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/08/artyoung_treesatnight7.jpg?resize=768%2C1208&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/08/artyoung_treesatnight7.jpg?resize=600%2C944&#38;ssl=1 600w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Drawing by Art Young from <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2019/08/06/trees-at-night-art-young/\"><em>Trees at Night</em></a>, 1926. (Available <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/last-appeal-from-trees-at-night-by-art-young_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a print</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>There is a way, with moderate moral imagination and considerable countercultural courage, to subvert this tendency without turning away from the reality and magnitude of suffering that we do live with &#8212; a way to esteem in attention and admiration not the unluckiness of what has happened to us but the luckiness that, despite it, we have become the people we are and have the lives we have by the sheer unwillingness to stay in that small dark place, which is at heart a willingness to be larger than our hurt selves. </p>\n<p>It is not a new way of reframing personal narrative (which, after all, is <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2018/01/15/oliver-sacks-identity-self-narrative/\">the neuropsychological pillar of identity</a>). It is a very old way, common to many of the world&#8217;s <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2015/11/06/alan-watts-swimming-headless/\">ancient traditions</a> but most clearly and creatively articulated by the Stoic philosopher <strong>Marcus Aurelius</strong> (April 26, 121&#8211;March 17, 180).</p>\n<figure  class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Meditations-Annotated-Marcus-Aurelius/dp/1541673859/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2014/10/marcusaurelius.jpg?w=680&#038;ssl=1\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\"></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Marcus Aurelius</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Because the modern mind calculates validity of vantage point by estimating the comparative value of suffering, it must be observed that, later in life, Marcus Aurelius had it easier than most of his contemporaries, being Emperor; it must also be observed that, earlier in life, he had it harder than most, being a <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2014/10/07/marcus-aurelius-meditations-father/\">fatherless child</a> and a <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2020/02/16/marcus-aurelius-in-love-amy-richlin/\">queer teenager</a> in Roman antiquity, epochs before the notion of LGBTQ rights, or for that matter most human rights. It is hardly surprising that he turned to Stoicism for succor and training in living with the uncertainty of events and the certainty of loss. </p>\n<p>His timeless <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Meditations-Annotated-Marcus-Aurelius/dp/1541673859/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><strong><em>Meditations</em></strong></a> (<a href=\"https://www.worldcat.org/title/meditations/oclc/1200832206&#038;referer=brief_results\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><em>public library</em></a>), newly translated and annotated by the British classics scholar Robin Waterfield, were the original self-help &#8212; Marcus wrote these notebooks primarily as notes to himself while learning how to live: how to live with more agency, equanimity, and even joy in a world violently unpredictable at all times and especially so in his time. </p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_73641\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/the-great-wave-off-kanagawa-by-hokusai-1831_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/greatwave_hokusai.jpg?resize=680%2C457&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"457\" class=\"size-full wp-image-73641\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/greatwave_hokusai.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/greatwave_hokusai.jpg?resize=320%2C215&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/greatwave_hokusai.jpg?resize=600%2C404&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/greatwave_hokusai.jpg?resize=240%2C161&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/06/greatwave_hokusai.jpg?resize=768%2C516&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\"><em>The Great Wave off Kanagawa</em> by Japanese artist Hokusai, 1831. (Available <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/the-great-wave-off-kanagawa-by-hokusai-1831_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a print</a> and <a href=\"https://society6.com/brainpicker/collection/vintage-science-face-masks?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a face mask</a>, benefitting The Nature Conservancy.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>In one of those self-counsels, Marcus Aurelius considers the key to regarding one&#8217;s own life, and living it, with positive realism:</p>\n<blockquote><p>Be like a headland: the waves beat against it continuously, but it stands fast and around it the boiling water dies down. &#8220;It&#8217;s my rotten luck that this has happened to me.&#8221; On the contrary, &#8220;It&#8217;s my good luck that, although this has happened to me, I still feel no distress, since I&#8217;m unbruised by the present and unconcerned about the future.&#8221; What happened could have happened to anyone, but not everyone could have carried on without letting it distress him. So why regard the incident as a piece of bad luck rather than seeing your avoidance of distress as a piece of good luck? Do you generally describe a person as unlucky when his nature worked well? Or do you count it as a malfunction of a person&#8217;s nature when it succeeds in securing the outcome it wanted?</p></blockquote>\n<figure id=\"attachment_73026\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/spring-moon-at-ninomiya-beach-by-hasui-kawase-1931_print?sku=s6-19564891p4a1v46?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase1.jpg?resize=680%2C1014&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"1014\" class=\"size-full wp-image-73026\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase1.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase1.jpg?resize=320%2C477&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase1.jpg?resize=600%2C895&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase1.jpg?resize=240%2C358&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase1.jpg?resize=768%2C1146&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hasuikawase1.jpg?resize=1030%2C1536&#38;ssl=1 1030w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\"><em>Spring Moon at Ninomiya Beach</em>, 1931 &#8212; one of Hasui Kawase&#8217;s <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2021/03/22/hasui-kawase-prints/\">vintage Japanese woodblocks</a>. (Available <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/spring-moon-at-ninomiya-beach-by-hasui-kawase-1931_print?sku=s6-19564891p4a1v46?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a print</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>With an eye to &#8220;what human nature wants&#8221; &#8212; what life ultimately demands as it lives itself through us, and what our highest answer is &#8212; he concludes:</p>\n<blockquote><p>Can what happened to you stop you from being fair, high-minded, moderate, conscientious, unhasty, honest, moral, self-reliant, and so on &#8212; from possessing all the qualities that, when present, enable a man&#8217;s<a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2014/10/17/ursula-k-le-guin-gender/\">*</a> nature to be fulfilled? So then, whenever something happens that might cause you distress, remember to rely on this principle: this is not bad luck, but bearing it valiantly is good luck.</p></blockquote>\n<p>Complement with an equally counterintuitive and perspective-broadening modern case for <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2021/07/25/richard-dawkins-death/\">the luckiness of death</a> and Alan Watts on <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2015/11/06/alan-watts-swimming-headless/\">the ambiguity of good and bad luck</a>, then revisit other highlights from the indispensable <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Meditations-Annotated-Marcus-Aurelius/dp/1541673859/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><strong><em>Meditations</em></strong></a>: Marcus Aurelius on <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2021/04/13/marcus-aurelius-meditations-robin-waterfield/\">how to handle disappointing people</a>, <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2019/05/20/marcus-aurelius-meditations-mortality-presence/\">the key to living with presence</a>, <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2017/01/03/marcus-aurelius-meditations-bed-work/\">the most potent motivation for work</a>, and <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2017/01/03/marcus-aurelius-meditations-bed-work/\">how to begin each day for maximum serenity of mind</a>.</p>\n<hr /><h3>donating = loving</h3><p class=\"flipboard-keep\">For 15 years, I have been spending hundreds of hours and thousands of dollars each month to keep <em>Brain Pickings</em> going. It has remained free and ad-free and alive thanks to patronage from readers. I have no staff, no interns, no assistant — a thoroughly one-woman labor of love that is also my life and my livelihood. 00:55:07","updatedTime":"2021-09-28 00:55:07","title":"The Blue Horses of Our Destiny: Artist Franz Marc, the Wisdom of Animals, and the Fight of Beauty Against Brutality","link":"https://www.brainpickings.org/?p=74334","description":"<h3>Tragedy and transcendence in the search for the spiritual in nature. </h3>\n<hr>\n<p><a href=\"http://www.amazon.com/Blue-Horses-Poems-Mary-Oliver/dp/1594204799/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img class=\"cover\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2015/02/maryoliver_bluehorses.jpg?w=680&#038;ssl=1\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a>“Do you need a prod? Do you need a little darkness to get you going?” wrote Mary Oliver in <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2015/02/09/mary-oliver-blue-horses-fourth-sign-of-the-zodiac/\">one</a> of the masterpiece from her suite of poems celebrating the urgency of aliveness, <a href=\"http://www.amazon.com/Blue-Horses-Poems-Mary-Oliver/dp/1594204799/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><strong><em>Blue Horses</em></strong></a> (<a href=\"http://www.worldcat.org/title/blue-horses/oclc/870919766&#038;referer=brief_results\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><em>public library</em></a>).</p>\n<p>In the bleak winter of 1916, in the thickest darkness of World War I, several enormous canvases dappled in pointillist patterns of color appeared across the French countryside, as if Kandinsky or Klee had descended upon the war-torn hills to bandage the brutality with beauty. But no. The painted tarps were military camouflage, designed to conceal artillery from aerial observation &#8212; the work of the young German painter, printmaker, and Expressionist pioneer <strong>Franz Marc</strong> (February 8, 1880&#8211;March 4, 1916), who had devoted himself to parting the veil of appearances with art in order to &#8220;look for and paint this inner, spiritual side of nature.&#8221;</p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_74340\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/deer-in-a-monastery-garden-by-franz-marc-1912_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/FranzMarc_DeerInAMonasteryGarden_sm.jpg?resize=680%2C513&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"513\" class=\"size-full wp-image-74340\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/FranzMarc_DeerInAMonasteryGarden_sm.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/FranzMarc_DeerInAMonasteryGarden_sm.jpg?resize=320%2C241&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/FranzMarc_DeerInAMonasteryGarden_sm.jpg?resize=600%2C453&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/FranzMarc_DeerInAMonasteryGarden_sm.jpg?resize=240%2C181&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/FranzMarc_DeerInAMonasteryGarden_sm.jpg?resize=768%2C579&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\"><em>Deer in a Monastery Garden</em>, 1912. (Available <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/deer-in-a-monastery-garden-by-franz-marc-1912_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a print</a> and as <a href=\"https://society6.com/brainpicker/cards?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">stationery cards</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Conscripted into the German Imperial Army at the outbreak of the war, midway through his thirties and just after a period of extraordinary creative fecundity, Marc found this improbable outlet for his artistic vitality during his military service. Unlikely to have had any practical advantage over ordinary camouflage, his colossal canvases are almost certain to have served as a psychological lifeline for the young artist drafted into the machinery of death.</p>\n<p>Within a month of painting them, Marc was dead &#8212; a shell explosion in the first days of the war&#8217;s longest battle sent a metal splinter into his skull, killing him instantly while a German government official was compiling a list of prominent artists to be recalled from military service as national treasures, with Marc&#8217;s name on it. </p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_74342\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/FranzMarc_TheFateOfTheAnimals.jpg?resize=680%2C498&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"498\" class=\"size-full wp-image-74342\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/FranzMarc_TheFateOfTheAnimals.jpg?w=1144&#38;ssl=1 1144w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/FranzMarc_TheFateOfTheAnimals.jpg?resize=320%2C234&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/FranzMarc_TheFateOfTheAnimals.jpg?resize=600%2C440&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/FranzMarc_TheFateOfTheAnimals.jpg?resize=240%2C176&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/FranzMarc_TheFateOfTheAnimals.jpg?resize=768%2C563&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\"><em>The Fate of the Animals</em>, 1913.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Among the paintings he produced in those two ecstatically prolific years just before he was drafted was <em>The Fate of the Animals</em> &#8212; an arresting depiction of the interplay of beauty and brutality, terror and tenderness, in the chaos of life. An inscription appeared under the canvas in Marc&#8217;s hand: “And all being is flaming agony.”</p>\n<p>Destroyed in a warehouse fire in 1916, <em>The Fate of the Animals</em> was restored by Marc&#8217;s close friend <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2020/09/24/paul-klee-tree-artist-creativity/\">Paul Klee</a>, who painstakingly recreated the oil canvas from surviving photographs. </p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_74339\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/the-tiger-by-franz-marc-1912_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/FranzMarc_TheTiger_sm.jpg?resize=680%2C752&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"752\" class=\"size-full wp-image-74339\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/FranzMarc_TheTiger_sm.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/FranzMarc_TheTiger_sm.jpg?resize=320%2C354&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/FranzMarc_TheTiger_sm.jpg?resize=600%2C664&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/FranzMarc_TheTiger_sm.jpg?resize=240%2C265&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/FranzMarc_TheTiger_sm.jpg?resize=768%2C849&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\"><em>The Tiger</em>, 1912. (Available <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/the-tiger-by-franz-marc-1912_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a print</a> and as <a href=\"https://society6.com/brainpicker/cards?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">stationery cards</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<figure id=\"attachment_74337\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/the-foxes-by-franz-marc-19135888917_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/FranzMarc_TheFoxes_sm.jpg?resize=680%2C929&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"929\" class=\"size-full wp-image-74337\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/FranzMarc_TheFoxes_sm.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/FranzMarc_TheFoxes_sm.jpg?resize=320%2C437&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/FranzMarc_TheFoxes_sm.jpg?resize=600%2C820&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/FranzMarc_TheFoxes_sm.jpg?resize=240%2C328&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/FranzMarc_TheFoxes_sm.jpg?resize=768%2C1049&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/FranzMarc_TheFoxes_sm.jpg?resize=1125%2C1536&#38;ssl=1 1125w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\"><em>The Foxes</em>, 1913. (Available <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/the-foxes-by-franz-marc-19135888917_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a print</a> and as <a href=\"https://society6.com/brainpicker/cards?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">stationery cards</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Animals, Marc felt, were in many ways superior to humans &#8212; more honest in their expression of their inner truths, in more direct contact with the inner truths of nature:</p>\n<blockquote><p>Animals with their virginal sense of life awakened all that was good in me.</p></blockquote>\n<figure id=\"attachment_74338\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/the-little-monkey-by-franz-marc-1912_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/FranzMarc_TheLittleMonkey_sm.jpg?resize=680%2C478&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"478\" class=\"size-full wp-image-74338\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/FranzMarc_TheLittleMonkey_sm.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/FranzMarc_TheLittleMonkey_sm.jpg?resize=320%2C225&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/FranzMarc_TheLittleMonkey_sm.jpg?resize=600%2C422&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/FranzMarc_TheLittleMonkey_sm.jpg?resize=240%2C169&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/FranzMarc_TheLittleMonkey_sm.jpg?resize=768%2C540&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\"><em>The Little Monkey</em>, 1912. (Available <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/the-little-monkey-by-franz-marc-1912_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a print</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<figure id=\"attachment_74336\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/the-large-blue-horses-by-franz-marc-1911_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/FranzMarc_LargeBlueHorses_sm.jpg?resize=680%2C389&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"389\" class=\"size-full wp-image-74336\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/FranzMarc_LargeBlueHorses_sm.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/FranzMarc_LargeBlueHorses_sm.jpg?resize=320%2C183&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/FranzMarc_LargeBlueHorses_sm.jpg?resize=600%2C343&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/FranzMarc_LargeBlueHorses_sm.jpg?resize=240%2C137&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/FranzMarc_LargeBlueHorses_sm.jpg?resize=768%2C439&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\"><em>The Large Blue Horses</em>, 1911. (Available <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/the-large-blue-horses-by-franz-marc-1911_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a print</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>In 1910, just before he turned thirty, Marc became a founding member of <em>The Blue Rider</em> &#8212; a journal that became an epicenter of the German Expressionist community that included artists like Kandinsky, who had just formalized his thinking on <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2014/06/02/kandinsky-concerning-the-spiritual-in-art/\">the role of the spiritual in art</a>, and Klee. At the end of that year, Marc began corresponding with the twenty-two-year-old writer and pianist Lisbeth Macke, who was married to one of the <em>Blue Rider</em> artists, about the relationship between color and emotion through the lens of music. Exactly a century after Goethe devised his <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2012/08/17/goethe-theory-of-colours/\">psychology of color and emotion</a>, Macke and Marc created a kind of synesthetic color wheel of tones, assigning sombre sounds to blue, joyful sounds to yellow, and a brutality of discord to red. Marc went on to ascribe not only emotional but spiritual attributes to the primary colors, writing to Macke:</p>\n<blockquote><p>Blue is the male principle, stern and spiritual. Yellow the female principle, gentle, cheerful and sensual. Red is matter, brutal and heavy and always the colour which must be fought and vanquished by the other two!</p></blockquote>\n<p>Further exploring the analogy between music and color, Marc envisioned the equivalent of music without tonality in painting &#8212; a sensibility where &#8220;a so-called dissonance is simply a consonance apart,&#8221; producing a harmonic effect in the overall composition, in color as in sound. </p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_74341\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/the-tower-of-blue-horses-by-franz-marc-1913_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/FranzMarc_TowerOfBlueHorses.jpg?resize=680%2C1081&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"1081\" class=\"size-full wp-image-74341\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/FranzMarc_TowerOfBlueHorses.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/FranzMarc_TowerOfBlueHorses.jpg?resize=320%2C509&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/FranzMarc_TowerOfBlueHorses.jpg?resize=600%2C954&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/FranzMarc_TowerOfBlueHorses.jpg?resize=240%2C381&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/FranzMarc_TowerOfBlueHorses.jpg?resize=768%2C1220&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/FranzMarc_TowerOfBlueHorses.jpg?resize=967%2C1536&#38;ssl=1 967w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\"><em>The Tower of Blue Horses</em>, 1913. (Available <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/the-tower-of-blue-horses-by-franz-marc-1913_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a print</a> and as <a href=\"https://society6.com/brainpicker/cards?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">stationery cards</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Twenty years after Marc&#8217;s death on the battlefields of the First World War, when the forces of terror that had fomented it festered into the Second, the Nazis declared his art &#8220;degenerate.&#8221; Many of his paintings went missing after WWII, last seen in a 1937 Nazi exhibition of &#8220;degenerate&#8221; art, alongside several of Klee&#8217;s paintings. Marc&#8217;s art is believed to have been seized by Nazi leaders for their personal theft-collections. An international search for his painting <em>The Tower of Blue Horses</em> has been underway for decades. In 2012, another of his missing paintings of horses was discovered in the Munich home of the son of one of Hitler&#8217;s art dealers, along with more than a thousand other artworks the Nazis denounced as &#8220;degenerate&#8221; in their deadly ideology but welcomed into their private living rooms as works of transcendent beauty and poetic power. </p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_74335\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/the-dreaming-horses-by-franz-marc-1913_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/FranzMarc_DreamingHorses_sm.jpg?resize=680%2C570&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"570\" class=\"size-full wp-image-74335\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/FranzMarc_DreamingHorses_sm.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/FranzMarc_DreamingHorses_sm.jpg?resize=320%2C268&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/FranzMarc_DreamingHorses_sm.jpg?resize=600%2C503&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/FranzMarc_DreamingHorses_sm.jpg?resize=240%2C201&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/FranzMarc_DreamingHorses_sm.jpg?resize=768%2C644&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\"><em>The Dreaming Horses</em>, 1913. (Available <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/the-dreaming-horses-by-franz-marc-1913_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a print</a> and as <a href=\"https://society6.com/brainpicker/cards?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">stationery cards</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>The title poem of Mary Oliver&#8217;s <a href=\"http://www.amazon.com/Blue-Horses-Poems-Mary-Oliver/dp/1594204799/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><strong><em>Blue Horses</em></strong></a> embodies the original meaning of empathy, which became popular in the early twentieth century as <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2016/12/14/you-must-change-rilke-rodin-empathy/\">a term for projecting oneself into a work of art</a>. The poet projects herself into Marc&#8217;s painting <em>The Large Blue Horses</em>, running her hand gently one animal&#8217;s blue mane, letting another&#8217;s nose touch her gently, as she reflects on Marc&#8217;s tragic, tremendous life that managed to make such timeless portals into beauty and tenderness in the midst of unspeakable brutality:</p>\n<blockquote><p>I do not know how to thank you, Franz Marc.<br />\nMaybe our world will grow kinder eventually.<br />\nMaybe the desire to make something beautiful<br />\nis the piece of God that is inside each of us.</p></blockquote>\n<hr /><h3>donating = loving</h3><p class=\"flipboard-keep\">For 15 years, I have been spending hundreds of hours and thousands of dollars each month to keep <em>Brain Pickings</em> going. It has remained free and ad-free and alive thanks to patronage from readers. I have no staff, no interns, no assistant — a thoroughly one-woman labor of love that is also my life and my livelihood.
