-55-34-300_a77a463ecfa8c33f.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/brainpickings/rss/~4/OB4d_KTbZoo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx3/cdn19@2020_4/2021/09/27/16-55-33-726_ece6df5d29abb9e5.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1632761707371},{"createdTime":"2021-09-28 00:55:07","updatedTime":"2021-09-28 00:55:07","title":"Bob Dylan on Vulnerability, the Meaning of Integrity, and Music as an Instrument of Truth","link":"https://www.brainpickings.org/?p=74235","description":"<h3>&#8220;You must be vulnerable to be sensitive to reality. And to me being vulnerable is just another way of saying that one has nothing more to lose.&#8221;</h3>\n<hr>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Listening-Interviews-1970-1989-Jonathan-Cott/dp/1517909015/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\"><img width=\"320\" height=\"484\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/listening_jonathancott.jpg?fit=320%2C484&#38;ssl=1\" class=\"cover alignright size-medium\" alt=\"Bob Dylan on Vulnerability, the Meaning of Integrity, and Music as an Instrument of Truth\" loading=\"lazy\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/listening_jonathancott.jpg?w=397&#38;ssl=1 397w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/listening_jonathancott.jpg?resize=320%2C484&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/listening_jonathancott.jpg?resize=240%2C363&#38;ssl=1 240w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 320px) 100vw, 320px\" /></a></p><p>Self-knowledge might be the most difficult of life&#8217;s rewards &#8212; the hardest to earn and the hardest to bear. To know yourself is to know that you are not an unassailable fixity amid the entropic storm of the universe but a set of fragilities in constant flux. To know yourself is to know that you are not invulnerable. </p>\n<p>The honest encounter with that vulnerability is the wellspring of art: Every artist&#8217;s art is their coping mechanism for the extreme sensitivity to aliveness that we call beauty &#8212; the transcendent and terrifying capacity to be moved by the world, to let something outside us stir deeply something within us. All great art &#8212; and only honest art can be great &#8212; is therefore the work of vulnerability and all integrity the function of fidelity to one&#8217;s fragilities. </p>\n<p>That is what <strong>Bob Dylan</strong> (b. May 24, 1941) addresses with his penetrating poetics of insight in a 1977 conversation with Jonathan Cott &#8212; that uncommonly sensitive and erudite <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/tag/jonathan-cott/\">investigator of uncommon minds</a>. </p>\n<figure  class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><a href=\"https://www.loc.gov/pictures/item/00649926/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2014/05/bobdylan1.jpg?w=680&#038;ssl=1\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Bob Dylan (Library of Congress)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Cott prefaces the conversation, included in his collection <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Listening-Interviews-1970-1989-Jonathan-Cott/dp/1517909015/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><strong><em>Listening: Interviews, 1970&#8211;1989</em></strong></a> (<a href=\"https://www.worldcat.org/title/listening-interviews-1970-1989/oclc/1107060820?referer=br&#038;ht=edition\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><em>public library</em></a>), with a soulful and percipient encapsulation of Dylan&#8217;s gift: </p>\n<blockquote><p>His songs are miracles, his ways mysterious and unfathomable. In words and music, he has reawakened, and thereby altered, our experience of the world. In statement (“He not busy being born is busy dying”) and in image (“My dreams are made of iron and steel / With a big bouquet / Of roses hanging down / From the heavens to the ground”) he has kept alive the idea of the poet and artist as <em>vates</em> &#8212; the visionary eye of the body politic &#8212; while keeping himself open to a conception of art that embraces and respects equally Charles Baudelaire and Charley Patton, Arthur Rimbaud and Smokey Robinson.</p></blockquote>\n<p>Dylan&#8217;s virtuosity with the mysterious and the miraculous has always sprung from his ethos of <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2014/05/21/bob-dylan-songwriters-on-songwriting-interview/\">placing the unconscious mind at the center of creativity</a>. In discussing his film <em>Renaldo and Clara</em> &#8212; which Dylan describes as being about integrity, about &#8220;naked alienation of the inner self against the outer self&#8221; &#8212; he tells Cott:</p>\n<blockquote><p>Human emotions are the great dictator.</p>\n<p>[&#8230;]</p>\n<p>You can’t be a slave to your emotions. If you’re a slave to your emotions you’re dependent on your emotions, and you’re only dealing with your conscious mind&#8230; You have to be faithful to your subconscious, unconscious, super-conscious &#8212; as well as to your conscious. Integrity is a facet of honesty. It has to do with knowing yourself.</p></blockquote>\n<p>True integrity necessitates the honesty of vulnerability &#8212; that great valve between us and the world, through which reality rushes into the chamber of our being and art pours out. Dylan observes:</p>\n<blockquote><p>You must be vulnerable to be sensitive to reality. And to me being vulnerable is just another way of saying that one has nothing more to lose. I don’t have anything but darkness to lose. I’m way beyond that.</p></blockquote>\n<figure  class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><a href=\"http://www.miltonglaser.com/the-work/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2012/06/miltonglaser_dylan.jpg?w=680&#038;ssl=1\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Bob Dylan by <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2013/06/26/milton-glaser-debbie-millman-interview/\">Milton Glaser</a>, 1967.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>When the conversation turns to humanity&#8217;s greatest spiritual sages &#8212; the teachers from various traditions best able to access and teach the eternal truths &#8212; Dylan counters Cott&#8217;s observation that &#8220;they speak and teach with more emotion,&#8221; redoubling his defiance of feeling as an organizing principle for truth:</p>\n<blockquote><p>I don’t believe in emotion. They use their hearts, their hearts don’t use them.</p></blockquote>\n<p>A generation after Aldous Huxley reverenced music as the great illuminator of the <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2016/04/05/aldous-huxley-music-at-night/\">&#8220;blessedness lying at the heart of things,&#8221;</a> Dylan exalts music as a supreme instrument of revelation: its inherent honesty, its elemental fidelity to truth &#8212; the temporal and the eternal, the personal and the universal:</p>\n<blockquote><p>Music is truthful&#8230; Music attracts the angels in the universe.</p></blockquote>\n<p>It may be that Bob Dylan is the Bach of our time &#8212; the rare vessel for universal truth, whose music contains <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2021/08/21/clemency-burton-hill-pablo-casals-albert-schweitzer-bach/\">“the ultimate expression of anything and everything.”</a></p>\n<p>Complement with three centuries of uncommon minds on <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2016/03/15/writers-on-music/\">the singular power of music</a> and Nick Cave on <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2019/01/24/nick-cave-music-ai/\">music, feeling, and transcendence</a>, then revisit psychologist Erich Fromm on <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2020/03/22/erich-fromm-revolution-of-hope/\">vulnerability as the key to our sanity</a>, philosopher Martha Nussbaum on <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2014/03/14/martha-nussbaum-bill-moyers-world-of-ideas/\">how to live with our human fragility</a>, and philosopher-poet Kahlil Gibran on <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2019/11/21/kahlil-gibran-prophet-talking/\">the courage to know yourself</a>.</p>\n<hr /><h3>donating = loving</h3><p class=\"flipboard-keep\">For 15 years, I have been spending hundreds of hours and thousands of dollars each month to keep <em>Brain Pickings</em> going. It has remained free and ad-free and alive thanks to patronage from readers. I have no staff, no interns, no assistant — a thoroughly one-woman labor of love that is also my life and my livelihood. If this labor makes your life more livable in any way, please consider aiding its sustenance with <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/donate/\">donation</a>.</p>\n\n<hr />\n\n<h3>newsletter</h3>\n<p>Brain Pickings has a free weekly newsletter. It comes out on Sundays and offers the week’s most inspiring reading. Here’s <a href=\"https://mailchi.mp/brainpickings/janna-levin-rebecca-elson-anne-lamott-james-gleick\">what to expect</a>. Like? <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/newsletter/\">Sign up.</a></p><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/brainpickings/rss/~4/Ntzeof6WZA8\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Fri, 27 Aug 2021 15:05:13 +0000","feedId":17,"bgimg":"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/listening_jonathancott.jpg?fit=320%2C484&ssl=1","linkMd5":"e2314c8106058ebc8d069b01d880be69","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn36@2020_5/2021/09/27/16-55-07-822_2e1080ddfed869b0.webp","destWidth":320,"destHeight":484,"sourceBytes":11892,"destBytes":11892,"author":"Maria Popova","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/listening_jonathancott.jpg?fit=320%2C484&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn36@2020_5/2021/09/27/16-55-07-822_2e1080ddfed869b0.webp","https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2014/05/bobdylan1.jpg?w=680&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn88@2020_1/2021/09/27/16-55-33-846_7eaf3439b26ab2ba.webp","https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2012/06/miltonglaser_dylan.jpg?w=680&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn93@2020_4/2021/09/27/16-55-33-209_2e95bf1b9e8533af.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/brainpickings/rss/~4/Ntzeof6WZA8":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn56@2020_2/2021/09/27/16-55-33-118_2e3a84885d7d94e7.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1632761707369},{"createdTime":"2021-09-28 00:55:07","updatedTime":"2021-09-28 00:55:07","title":"Consciousness and the Nature of the Universe: How Panpsychism and Its Fault Lines Shade in the Ongoing Mystery of What We Are","link":"https://www.brainpickings.org/?p=74136","description":"<h3>&#8220;We’ve barely begun to understand our place in the cosmos. As we continue to look out from our planet and contemplate the nature of reality, we should remember that there is a mystery right here where we stand.&#8221;</h3>\n<hr>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Conscious-Brief-Guide-Fundamental-Mystery/dp/0062906712/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\"><img width=\"320\" height=\"485\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/conscious_annakaharris.jpg?fit=320%2C485&#38;ssl=1\" class=\"cover alignright size-medium\" alt=\"Consciousness and the Nature of the Universe: How Panpsychism and Its Fault Lines Shade in the Ongoing Mystery of What We Are\" loading=\"lazy\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/conscious_annakaharris.jpg?w=1600&#38;ssl=1 1600w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/conscious_annakaharris.jpg?resize=320%2C485&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/conscious_annakaharris.jpg?resize=600%2C910&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/conscious_annakaharris.jpg?resize=240%2C364&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/conscious_annakaharris.jpg?resize=768%2C1165&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/conscious_annakaharris.jpg?resize=1013%2C1536&#38;ssl=1 1013w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/conscious_annakaharris.jpg?resize=1350%2C2048&#38;ssl=1 1350w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 320px) 100vw, 320px\" /></a></p><p>&#8220;Meditate often on the interconnectedness and mutual interdependence of all things in the universe,&#8221; the aging Marcus Aurelius <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2016/10/18/the-daily-stoic-ryan-holiday/\">instructed</a>. </p>\n<p>&#8220;Any live mind today is of the very same stuff as Plato’s &#038; Euripides,&#8221; the young Virginia Woolf <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2020/01/23/virginia-woolf-genius-and-ink-reading/\">meditated in her diary</a> two millennia later. &#8220;It is this common mind that binds the whole world together; &#038; all the world is mind.&#8221; </p>\n<p>Two years earlier, in the first year of the twentieth century and the final year of his life, the uncommonly minded Canadian psychiatrist Maurice Bucke had formalized this notion in his visionary, controversial book <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2019/04/11/cosmic-consciousness-maurice-bucke/\"><em>Cosmic Consciousness: A Study in the Evolution of the Human Mind</em></a>, which influenced generations of thinkers ranging from Albert Einstein to Abraham Maslow to Steve Jobs. </p>\n<p>Bucke himself had been greatly influenced by, then befriended and in turn influenced, Walt Whitman &#8212; a poet enraptured by <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2020/12/16/on-the-beach-alone-at-night-walt-whitman/\">how science illuminates the interconnectedness of life</a>, who contemplated the strangest and most paradoxical byproduct of consciousness <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2016/06/24/walt-whitman-democratic-vistas-self/\">&#8220;lifted out from all else, calm, like the stars, shining eternal&#8221;</a>: our sense of self.</p>\n<p>Science was young then &#8212; it still is &#8212; and the world was old, and the mind was old, its dwelling-place practically unchanged since the cranium of early <em>Homo sapiens</em> began accommodating a brain comparable to our own some three hundred thousand years ago. With neuroscience <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2017/02/23/beautiful-brain-santiago-ramon-y-cajal/\">yet to be born</a>, it fell on the poets and the philosophers to meditate on the complexities of consciousness &#8212; the sole valve between reality and our experience, made of the same matter as the stars. Today, neuroscience remains a young and insecure science, as crude as Galilean astronomy &#8212; and as revolutionary in the revelations it has already contoured, yet to be shaded in with the nuances of understanding that might, just might, one day illuminate the fundaments of consciousness.</p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_74144\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/art-from-the-principles-of-light-and-color-by-edwin-d-babbitt-18785730325_print?sku=s6-21454782p4a1v1?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/babbit5_small.jpg?resize=680%2C642&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"642\" class=\"size-full wp-image-74144\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/babbit5_small.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/babbit5_small.jpg?resize=320%2C302&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/babbit5_small.jpg?resize=600%2C567&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/babbit5_small.jpg?resize=240%2C227&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/babbit5_small.jpg?resize=768%2C725&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Plate from <em>The Principles of Light and Color: Including Among Other Things the Harmonic Laws of the Universe, the Etherio-atomic Philosophy of Force, Chromo Chemistry, Chromo Therapeutics, and the General Philosophy of the Fine Forces, Together with Numerous Discoveries and Practical Applications</em> by Edwin D. Babbitt, 1878. (Available as <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/art-from-the-principles-of-light-and-color-by-edwin-d-babbitt-18785730325_print?sku=s6-21454782p4a1v1?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">a print</a> and as <a href=\"https://society6.com/brainpicker/collection/vintage-science-cards?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">stationery cards</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Until that day comes, we have a panoply of theories about what it is that flickers on the cave walls of the cranium to irradiate our entire experience of life and reality. The most compelling &#8212; and the most controversial &#8212; of them are what <strong>Annaka Harris</strong> examines with equal parts openhearted curiosity and intelligent consideration in <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Conscious-Brief-Guide-Fundamental-Mystery/dp/0062906712/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><strong><em>Conscious: A Brief Guide to the Fundamental Mystery of the Mind</em></strong></a> (<a href=\"https://www.worldcat.org/title/conscious-a-brief-guide-to-the-fundamental-mystery-of-the-mind/oclc/1136872839&#038;referer=brief_results\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><em>public library</em></a>).</p>\n<p>At the center of her inquiry is an idea ancient Eastern spiritual traditions, a century of Western neurocognitive science, and epochs of philosophy share: the illusory nature of the self &#8212; the self that is always in flux yet <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2019/07/19/altered-states-of-consciousness-marc-wittmann/\">rooted in our experience of time</a>, the self we build and rebuild <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2018/01/15/oliver-sacks-identity-self-narrative/\">upon a narrative foundation</a>, the self separated from the other by <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2018/10/25/lewis-thomas-the-medusa-and-the-snail-self/\">a marvelously permeable boundary</a>, the self of which nature can so easily and profoundly <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2020/09/15/helen-macdonald-vesper-flights-eclipse/\">strip us during a solar eclipse</a>, the self into which we fortress our whole sense of identity and from which we peer out to receive our whole view of the world, only to discover again and again that the fortress is an appearance in consciousness filled with what Borges called <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2017/04/03/the-nothingness-of-personality-borges/\">&#8220;the nothingness of personality.&#8221;</a></p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_60067\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2017/02/23/beautiful-brain-santiago-ramon-y-cajal/\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/02/BeautifulBrain_p064.jpg?resize=680%2C887&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"887\" class=\"size-full wp-image-60067\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/02/BeautifulBrain_p064.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/02/BeautifulBrain_p064.jpg?resize=240%2C313&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/02/BeautifulBrain_p064.jpg?resize=320%2C417&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/02/BeautifulBrain_p064.jpg?resize=768%2C1002&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/02/BeautifulBrain_p064.jpg?resize=600%2C783&#38;ssl=1 600w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">One of neuroscience founding father Santiago Ramón y Cajal&#8217;s <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2017/02/23/beautiful-brain-santiago-ramon-y-cajal/\">little-known drawings of the brain</a>.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Drawing on the intricate neurological processes and disorders that shape and misshape our conscious experience, on the behavior-altering effects various parasites have on their hosts, and on her own experience of staggering changes in preference, habit, and temperament on the hormonal cocktail of pregnancy, Harris writes:</p>\n<blockquote><p>The idea that “I” am the ultimate source of my desires and actions begins to crumble [and] it’s hard to see how our behavior, preferences, and even choices could be under the control of our conscious will in any real sense. It seems much more accurate to say that consciousness is along for the ride &#8212; watching the show, rather than creating or controlling it. In theory, we can go as far as to say that few (if any) of our behaviors need consciousness in order to be carried out. But at an intuitive level, we assume that because human beings act in certain ways and are conscious &#8212; and because experiences such as fear, love, and pain feel like such powerful motivators within consciousness &#8212; our behaviors are driven by our awareness of them and otherwise would not occur.</p></blockquote>\n<p>And yet, she observes, many of the actions we attribute to consciousness and hold up as proof of it could, in theory, take place without consciousness, in a machine programmed to operate by logical sequences resulting in those selfsame actions. (That, after all, is <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2021/08/14/analogia-george-dyson/\">the most thrilling and terrifying question of artificial intelligence</a>.) She posits a curious meta-exception:</p>\n<blockquote><p>Consciousness seems to play a role in behavior <em>when we think and talk about the mystery of consciousness</em>. When I contemplate “what it’s like” to be something, that experience of consciousness presumably affects the subsequent processing taking place in my brain. And almost nothing I think or say when contemplating consciousness would make any sense coming from a system without it.</p>\n<p>[&#8230;]</p>\n<p>When I talk about the mystery of consciousness &#8212; referring to something I can distinguish and wonder about and attribute (or not) to other entities &#8212; it seems highly unlikely that I would ever do this, let alone devote so much time to it, without feeling the experience I am referring to (for the qualitative experience is the entire subject, and without it, I can have no knowledge of it whatsoever). And when I turn these ideas over in my mind, the fact that my thoughts are <em>about the experience of consciousness</em> suggests that there is a feedback loop of sorts and that consciousness is affecting my brain processing.</p></blockquote>\n<p>What emerges is the intimation that we are not merely machines that think &#8212; after all, many of our machines now &#8220;think&#8221; in the sense of processing information and adapting it to govern behavior &#8212; but machines that think about thinking, lending our biochemical machinery an edge of the miraculous not (yet) explicable by our science, which remains our mightiest technology of thought. She observes:</p>\n<blockquote><p>Most of our intuitions about what qualifies as evidence of consciousness affecting a system don’t survive scrutiny. Therefore, we must reevaluate the assumptions we tend to make about the role consciousness plays in driving behavior, as these assumptions naturally lead to the conclusions we draw about what consciousness is and what causes it to arise in nature. Everything we hope to uncover through consciousness studies &#8212; from determining whether or not a given person is in a conscious state, to pinpointing where in the evolution of life consciousness first emerged, to understanding the exact physical process that gives birth to conscious experience &#8212; is informed by our intuitions about the function of consciousness.</p></blockquote>\n<p>Where our intuitions break down most dramatically and where the breakdown most disorients us is in what may be the most poorly branded and therefore poorly understood theory of consciousness: panpsychism.</p>\n<figure  class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2016/02/29/arthur-rackham-brothers-grimm/\"><img src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2016/02/arthurrackham_grimm5.jpg\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Art by Arthur Rackham for a <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2016/02/29/arthur-rackham-brothers-grimm/\">rare 1917 edition</a> of the Brothers Grimm fairy tales. (Available <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/art-by-arthur-rackham-from-a-rare-1917-edition-of-the-brothers-grimm-fairy-tales_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a print</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Coined in the sixteenth century by the Italian philosopher and proto-scientist Francesco Patrizi, whose work inspired Galileo, from the Greek <em>pan</em> (“all”) and <em>psyche</em> (“mind” or “spirit”), panpsychism is the idea that all matter is endowed with the capacity for subjective experience of immaterial quality &#8212; the sort of experience we call, in its expression familiar to us, consciousness. </p>\n<p>In the epochs since, as the world slowly began shedding the cloth of the supernatural and began seeking in mystical notions a kernel of secular and scientifically verifiable truth, panpsychism came closer and closer to information theory and the modern scientific understanding of the physicality of the universe. (There are echoes of panpsychism in the great theoretical physicist John Archibald Wheeler&#8217;s famous <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2016/09/02/it-from-bit-wheeler/\">&#8220;It-for-Bit&#8221; theory</a>, asserting that &#8220;observer-participancy gives rise to information&#8221; because &#8220;all things physical are information-theoretic in origin and this is a participatory universe.&#8221;)</p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_68583\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/polychromatic-fringes-from-le-monde-physique-1882_print?sku=s6-11476452p4a1v1?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/08/1.jpg?resize=680%2C1083&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"1083\" class=\"size-full wp-image-68583\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/08/1.jpg?w=2245&#38;ssl=1 2245w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/08/1.jpg?resize=240%2C382&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/08/1.jpg?resize=320%2C510&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/08/1.jpg?resize=768%2C1224&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/08/1.jpg?resize=600%2C956&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/08/1.jpg?w=1360&#38;ssl=1 1360w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/08/1.jpg?w=2040&#38;ssl=1 2040w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Plate from <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2019/08/20/amedee-guillemin-le-monde-physique/\"><em>Le monde physique</em></a> by Amédée Guillemin, 1882. (Available as <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/polychromatic-fringes-from-le-monde-physique-1882_print?sku=s6-11476452p4a1v1?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">a print</a>, as a <a href=\"https://society6.com/brainpicker/collection/vintage-science-face-masks?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">face mask</a>, and as <a href=\"https://society6.com/brainpicker/collection/vintage-science-cards?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">stationery cards</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>With an eye to the muddling, misconstrual, and ample misapplications of panpsychism as a framework that could broaden the conversation on consciousness but instead often shuts it down, Harris does the essential and courageous public service of lens-clearing:</p>\n<blockquote><p>Those of us who want to push this conversation forward have an important obligation to clearly distinguish panpsychic views from the false conclusions people tend to draw from them &#8212; namely, that panpsychism somehow justifies or explains a variety of psychic phenomena &#8212; following from the incorrect assumption that consciousness must entail a mind with a single point of view and complex thoughts. Ascribing some level of consciousness to plants or inanimate matter is not the same as ascribing to them <em>human</em> minds with wishes and intentions like our own. Anyone who believes the universe has a plan for us or that he can consult with his “higher self” for medical advice should not feel propped up by the modern view of panpsychism.</p>\n<p>[&#8230;]</p>\n<p>Unfortunately, it seems quite hard for us to drop the intuition that consciousness equals complex thought. But if consciousness is in fact a more basic aspect of the universe than previously believed, that doesn’t suddenly give credence to your neighbor’s belief that she can communicate telepathically with her ficus tree. In actuality, if a version of panpsychism is correct, everything will still appear to us and behave exactly as it already does.</p></blockquote>\n<figure id=\"attachment_74145\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/art-from-the-principles-of-light-and-color-by-edwin-d-babbitt-18785730339_print?sku=s6-21454807p4a1v1?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/babbit1_small.jpg?resize=680%2C933&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"933\" class=\"size-full wp-image-74145\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/babbit1_small.jpg?w=1050&#38;ssl=1 1050w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/babbit1_small.jpg?resize=320%2C439&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/babbit1_small.jpg?resize=600%2C823&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/babbit1_small.jpg?resize=240%2C329&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/babbit1_small.jpg?resize=768%2C1053&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Plate from <em>The Principles of Light and Color</em> by Edwin D. Babbitt, 1878. (Available as <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/art-from-the-principles-of-light-and-color-by-edwin-d-babbitt-18785730339_print?sku=s6-21454807p4a1v1?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">a print</a> and as <a href=\"https://society6.com/brainpicker/collection/vintage-science-cards?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">stationery cards</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Such appropriations of panpsychism are to the study of consciousness what the pseudoscience of phrenology is to neuroscience &#8212; contours of promising regions of exploration on our ever-evolving map of reality, shaded in with human bias. Rather than having the egalitarian view of consciousness-across-matter they seek to espouse, these misinterpretations impose on the concept of consciousness self-referential standards rife with human exceptionalism, making of nature an uncanny valley that betrays both nature and our humanity. </p>\n<p>Paradoxically, this misunderstanding of panpsychism is often used as an argument against panpsychism itself, not against its misunderstanding. But to actually consider a lichen or a quark endowed with a measure of consciousness is to recognize that its experience cannot, by structural definition, be anything close to our subjective human experience of consciousness &#8212; our <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2017/05/25/christof-koch-consciousness-qualia/\">qualia</a> and their byproduct: the sense of self. </p>\n<p>Considering what might be the greatest intuitive challenge to psychism, known as the &#8220;combination problem&#8221; &#8212; how the small constituents of matter, each the carrier of primitive consciousness, can combine into larger entities that have new and different consciousnesses, including ours &#8212; Harris observes that much of the challenge stems from a reflexive confusion:</p>\n<blockquote><p>For many scientists and philosophers, the combination problem presents the biggest obstacle to accepting any description of reality that includes consciousness as a widespread feature. However, the obstacle we face here once again seems to be a case of confusing <em>consciousness</em> with the concept of a <em>self</em>, as philosophers and scientists tend to speak in terms of a “subject” of consciousness. The term “self” is usually used to describe a more complex set of psychological characteristics &#8212; including qualities such as self-confidence or a capacity for empathy &#8212; but a “subject” still describes an experience of self in its most basic form&#8230; Perhaps it’s wrong to talk about a subject of consciousness, and it’s more accurate to instead talk about the <em>content available</em> to conscious experience at any given location in space-time, determined by the matter present there &#8212; <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2015/01/16/dog-raincoat-alexandra-horowitz/\">umwelts</a> applied not just to organisms, but to all matter, in every configuration and at every point in space-time.</p></blockquote>\n<p>Iris Murdoch &#8212; one of the most brilliant and underappreciated philosophical minds our species has produced &#8212; provided a potent antidote to the combination problem in her lovely notion of <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2019/10/21/iris-murdoch-unselfing/\"><em>unselfing</em></a>, rooted in the recognition that &#8220;the self, the place where we live, is a place of illusion.&#8221; In this light, the combination problem becomes decidedly less problematic &#8212; without the notion of a subject, a concrete entity to be combined with another concrete entity, there is no combining to be done. Consciousness becomes both the vessel of experience and the content of experience, and transcends both &#8212; more field than form. </p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_72735\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/art-from-thomas-wrights-an-original-theory-or-new-hypothesis-of-the-universe-17504457506_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/thomaswright6.jpg?resize=680%2C753&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"753\" class=\"size-full wp-image-72735\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/thomaswright6.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/thomaswright6.jpg?resize=240%2C266&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/thomaswright6.jpg?resize=320%2C354&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/thomaswright6.jpg?resize=768%2C850&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/thomaswright6.jpg?resize=600%2C664&#38;ssl=1 600w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Plate from <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2021/02/16/thomas-wright-original-theory/\"><em>An Original Theory or New Hypothesis of the Universe</em></a> by Thomas Wright, 1750. (Available as <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/art-from-thomas-wrights-an-original-theory-or-new-hypothesis-of-the-universe-17504457506_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">a print</a>, as a <a href=\"https://society6.com/brainpicker/collection/vintage-science-face-masks?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">face mask</a>, and as <a href=\"https://society6.com/brainpicker/collection/vintage-science-cards?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">stationery cards</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>After citing research on split-brain patients, in whom mental function and the contents of consciousness can be divided in astonishing ways, Harris writes:</p>\n<blockquote><p>[Without a self], consciousness could persist as is, while the character and content change, depending on the arrangement of the specific matter in question. Maybe content is sometimes shared across large, intricately connected regions and sometimes confined to very small ones, perhaps even overlapping. If two human brains were connected, both people might feel as if the content of their consciousness had simply expanded, with each person feeling a continuous transformation from the content of one person to the whole of the two, until the connection was more or less complete. It’s only when you insert the concepts of “him,” “her,” “you,” and “me” as discrete entities that the expanding of content for any area of consciousness (or even multiple areas merging) becomes a combination problem.</p></blockquote>\n<p>Harris ends her rigorous reconnaissance mission of the terra semicognita of consciousness studies with the telescopic perspective that is the poetry of possibility:</p>\n<blockquote><p>Humanity is young, and we’ve barely begun to understand our place in the cosmos. As we continue to look out from our planet and contemplate the nature of reality, we should remember that there is a mystery right here where we stand.</p></blockquote>\n<p>A century ago &#8212; a century during which humanity split the atom, unraveled the mysteries of our genetic code, and heard the sound of spacetime for the first time &#8212; quantum theory originator Max Planck insisted that <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2019/06/12/max-planck-where-is-science-going/\">&#8220;science cannot solve the ultimate mystery of nature&#8230; because&#8230; we ourselves are part of nature and therefore part of the mystery that we are trying to solve.”</a> In the first year of that century, Lord Kelvin took the podium at the British Association of Science to declare that “there is nothing new to be discovered in physics,&#8221; while at the same moment, a young patent clerk in Zurich was incubating the ideas that would converge into his theory of relativity, forever transfiguring our elemental understanding of reality. It is our human nature to consider the inconceivable impossible, again and again mistaking the parameters of the conceivable for the perimeter of the possible. But it is also the nature of the human mind &#8212; that material miracle of electrical and poetic impulses &#8212; to transcend its own limits of imagination again and again, inventing new parameters of thought that broaden the perimeter of the possible until it becomes real. </p>\n<p>Complement <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Conscious-Brief-Guide-Fundamental-Mystery/dp/0062906712/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><strong><em>Conscious</em></strong></a> with <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2021/06/13/alan-lightman-probable-impossibilities/\"><em>Probable Impossibilities</em></a> &#8212; physicist Alan Lightman&#8217;s poetic meditation on what makes life worth living &#8212; then revisit William James&#8217;s foundational work on <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2018/06/04/william-james-varieties-consciousness/\">consciousness and the four features of transcendent experiences</a>.</p>\n<hr /><h3>donating = loving</h3><p class=\"flipboard-keep\">For 15 years, I have been spending hundreds of hours and thousands of dollars each month to keep <em>Brain Pickings</em> going. It has remained free and ad-free and alive thanks to patronage from readers. I have no staff, no interns, no assistant — a thoroughly one-woman labor of love that is also my life and my livelihood. If this labor makes your life more livable in any way, please consider aiding its sustenance with <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/donate/\">donation</a>.</p>\n\n<hr />\n\n<h3>newsletter</h3>\n<p>Brain Pickings has a free weekly newsletter. +0000","feedId":17,"bgimg":"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/conscious_annakaharris.jpg?fit=320%2C485&ssl=1","linkMd5":"7406c47f0684b1b025674cb6de9b43ac","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn15@2020_5/2021/09/27/16-55-25-642_2dfb6afd48d5afd5.webp","destWidth":320,"destHeight":485,"sourceBytes":39090,"destBytes":39090,"author":"Maria Popova","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/conscious_annakaharris.jpg?fit=320%2C485&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn15@2020_5/2021/09/27/16-55-25-642_2dfb6afd48d5afd5.webp","https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/babbit5_small.jpg?resize=680%2C642&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn47@2020_4/2021/09/27/16-55-35-680_7dcf65efa49e29d9.webp","https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/02/BeautifulBrain_p064.jpg?resize=680%2C887&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn3@2020_6/2021/09/27/16-55-34-220_329cbf53743b055a.webp","https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2016/02/arthurrackham_grimm5.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn100@2020_5/2021/09/27/16-55-33-280_a6539457c5aefeed.webp","https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/08/1.jpg?resize=680%2C1083&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn41@2020_4/2021/09/27/16-55-33-340_5d25897bbe14b497.webp","https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/babbit1_small.jpg?resize=680%2C933&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn20@2020_4/2021/09/27/16-55-35-705_916ae345546882b5.webp","https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/thomaswright6.jpg?resize=680%2C753&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx31/cdn56@2020_4/2021/09/27/16-55-35-674_4f8b36518bd347ea.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/brainpickings/rss/~4/MblFb-W0ZUU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn36@2020_6/2021/09/27/16-55-33-856_2c93b542157dd7e4.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1632761707375},{"createdTime":"2021-09-28 00:55:07","updatedTime":"2021-09-28 00:55:07","title":"Love, Death, and Whitman: Poet Mark Doty on the Paradox of Desire and the Courage to Love Against the Certitude of Loss","link":"https://www.brainpickings.org/?p=74467","description":"<h3>&#8220;Isn’t the flesh a way to drink of the fountain of otherhood, a way to taste the not-I, a way to blur the edges and thus feel the fact of them?&#8230; You need to both remember where love leads and love anyway; you can both see the end of desire and be consumed by it all at once.&#8221;</h3>\n<hr>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/What-Grass-Walt-Whitman-Life/dp/039354141X/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\"><img width=\"320\" height=\"481\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/whatisthegrass_markdoty_whitman.jpg?fit=320%2C481&#38;ssl=1\" class=\"cover alignright size-medium\" alt=\"Love, Death, and Whitman: Poet Mark Doty on the Paradox of Desire and the Courage to Love Against the Certitude of Loss\" loading=\"lazy\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/whatisthegrass_markdoty_whitman.jpg?w=799&#38;ssl=1 799w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/whatisthegrass_markdoty_whitman.jpg?resize=320%2C481&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/whatisthegrass_markdoty_whitman.jpg?resize=600%2C901&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/whatisthegrass_markdoty_whitman.jpg?resize=240%2C360&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/09/whatisthegrass_markdoty_whitman.jpg?resize=768%2C1153&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 320px) 100vw, 320px\" /></a></p><p>Love and death come to us on common terms &#8212; unbidden and total, impervious to protest, naked of pretension. They also come to us entwined: Every love is a franchise of grief, for to love anything is to accept its loss &#8212; by a dissipation of ardor or of atoms, the atoms constellating the beloved or the atoms constellating us and the consciousness that does the loving, certain to one day go the way of every other consciousness and every other love that ever was and ever will be. </p>\n<p>In some deep sense, this inevitability of loss is precisely what makes love so ecstatic &#8212; a concentrated experience of aliveness consecrated by its own perishability. </p>\n<p>Walt Whitman touched on this with his tender, unflinching hand when he asked, &#8220;What indeed is beautiful, except Death and Love?&#8221;; when he observed that &#8220;to die is different from what any one supposed, and luckier.&#8221; He meant, I think, the luckiness of having lived at all, for death is only possible where life, <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2021/07/25/richard-dawkins-death/\">improbable against the austere odds of the universe</a>, once existed. </p>\n<p>That inescapable interplay is what poet <strong>Mark Doty</strong> explores throughout his incandescent book <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/What-Grass-Walt-Whitman-Life/dp/039354141X/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><strong><em>What Is the Grass: Walt Whitman in My Life</em></strong></a> (<a href=\"https://www.worldcat.org/title/what-is-the-grass-walt-whitman-in-my-life/oclc/1155086085&#038;referer=brief_results\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><em>public library</em></a>) &#8212; part biography, part memoir, part lyric meditation on life, love, and their consanguinity with death.</p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_64202\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/two-fishes-swimming-in-the-sea-not-more-lawless-than-we_framed-print?sku=s6-8967304p21a12v52a13v54?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2018/04/margaretcook_leavesofgrass6.jpg?resize=768%2C616&#038;ssl=1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Illustration by Margaret C. Cook for a <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2018/04/11/leaves-of-grass-margaret-cook/\">rare 1913 edition</a> of Walt Whitman&#8217;s <em>Leaves of Grass</em>. (Available <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/two-fishes-swimming-in-the-sea-not-more-lawless-than-we_framed-print?sku=s6-8967304p21a12v52a13v54?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a print</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Noting how deeply Whitman &#8212; the self-anointed <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2020/02/25/neri-oxman-walt-whitman/\">poet of the body and poet of the soul</a> &#8212; &#8220;understood that the particular is always perishing, and therefore all the more to be cherished,&#8221; Doty considers the body as an instrument of temporality and cherishment, through which the song of life sings itself and binds us to the chorus of all other bodies: </p>\n<blockquote><p>Begin with the body: water, vapor, air. You’re the shore on which an ocean of air is constantly breaking, in waves of breath. “Inside” and “outside” of lungs, permeable boundary of skin, eyes, ears, nose, holes in the body for substance passing in and out, no stable and fixed entity that is you, but a moving set of points through which pass water, air, light, food, parts of the bodies of others: their breath, tongues, genitals, hands. </p>\n<p>[&#8230;]</p>\n<p>The world enters us and departs, just as language and image and idea are imprinted upon our consciousness, considered, forgotten, passed on, released.</p></blockquote>\n<p>This perishable, permeable body, with its ceaseless entropic flow, lies at the heart of the paradox of desire &#8212; that electric impulse felt in the Body and felt in the Soul, furnishing our most palpable evidence that the two are one. “Behold,&#8221; Whitman wrote, &#8220;the body includes and is the meaning, the main concern and includes and is the soul.” And so desire becomes a sacrament to the interleaving of love and death, temporal by definition and necessity, its temporality the wellspring of its delirium. </p>\n<p>Awake to this fundament of feeling, Doty challenges the damaging Romantic ideal of interminable desire within any given love &#8212; a concept by nature self-negating, dishonoring the very thing that gives desire its electric charge:</p>\n<blockquote><p>Even in the imagined paradise of limitless eros, there must be room for death; otherwise the endlessness, the lack of limit or of boundary, finally drains things of their tension, removes all edges&#8230; The same body that strains toward freedom and escape also has outer edges, also exists in time, and it’s that doubling that makes the body the sexy and troubling thing it is. O taste and see. Isn’t the flesh a way to drink of the fountain of otherhood, a way to taste the not-I, a way to blur the edges and thus feel the fact of them?</p></blockquote>\n<figure id=\"attachment_64208\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/how-calm-how-solemn-it-grows-to-ascend-the-atmosphere-of-lovers_print?sku=s6-8967910p4a1v45?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2018/04/margaretcook_leavesofgrass10.jpg?resize=680%2C899&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"899\" class=\"size-full wp-image-64208\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2018/04/margaretcook_leavesofgrass10.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2018/04/margaretcook_leavesofgrass10.jpg?resize=240%2C317&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2018/04/margaretcook_leavesofgrass10.jpg?resize=320%2C423&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2018/04/margaretcook_leavesofgrass10.jpg?resize=768%2C1015&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2018/04/margaretcook_leavesofgrass10.jpg?resize=600%2C793&#38;ssl=1 600w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Art by Margaret C. Cook from <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2018/04/11/leaves-of-grass-margaret-cook/\">the 1913 English edition</a> of <em>Leaves of Grass</em>. (Available <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/how-calm-how-solemn-it-grows-to-ascend-the-atmosphere-of-lovers_print?sku=s6-8967910p4a1v45?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a print</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>The longing of the ephemeral body is the Borgesian mirror in which the eternal longing of the soul is endlessly reflected and reflected back, flickering with the bittersweet beauty of our mortal destiny, with the transcendent urgency of life and love. Doty writes:</p>\n<blockquote><p>You need to both remember where love leads and love anyway; you can both see the end of desire and be consumed by it all at once. The ecstatic body’s a place to feel timelessness and to hear, ear held close to the chest of another, the wind that blows in there, hurrying us ahead and away, and to understand that this awareness does not put an end to longing but lends to it a shadow that is, in the late hour, beautiful.</p></blockquote>\n<p>With an eye to Whitman&#8217;s central credo, staked on the poet&#8217;s ethos that <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/2018/11/01/figuring/\">&#8220;every atom belonging to me as good belongs to you&#8221;</a> and that we are therefore not separate selves but contiguous territories of aliveness made all the more alive and more contiguous by love, Doty writes:</p>\n<blockquote><p>When the Self dissolves into a world of separate selves and death becomes real, love becomes a pact with grief; what is gained then is the inescapably poignant fact of individuality. There will never be another you, and I love the stubborn particularity of you because you will disappear.</p></blockquote>\n<figure id=\"attachment_69014\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/every-atom-belonging-to-me-as-good-belongs-to-you-art-by-lia-halloran-for-the-universe-in-verse2373447_framed-print?sku=s6-11773478p21a12v61a13v58?curator=brainpicker\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/10/Lia_1200.jpg?resize=680%2C680&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"680\" class=\"size-full wp-image-69014\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/10/Lia_1200.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/10/Lia_1200.jpg?resize=240%2C240&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/10/Lia_1200.jpg?resize=320%2C320&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/10/Lia_1200.jpg?resize=768%2C768&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i2.wp.com/www.brainpickings.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/10/Lia_1200.jpg?resize=600%2C600&#38;ssl=1 600w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Art by Lia Halloran for <a href=\"https://www.brainpickings.org/the-universe-in-verse/\"><em>The Universe in Verse</em></a>.
